Denial of Non-Mutawatir and Takfir
Analyzing whether denying non-mutawatir recitation constitutes kufr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that denial of a daruri matter is kufr, but such denial is excused when based on strong doubt (shubha) and plausible interpretation (ta'wil).

Core Idea
Denial of a daruri leads to kufr; strong doubt and interpretation excuse the denier.

This passage tackles a critical question in Hanafi usul: when does denial of a religious matter cross into disbelief? The author clarifies that the key factor is whether the matter is 'daruri' (self-evident and definitively known). However, even for matters that are definitively proven, if a person has a legitimate interpretative doubt, they are excused. The practical example of Imam Ali (RA) and the Khawarij illustrates this principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling about daruri matters
Find the statement that denial of something 'daruri' necessitates disbelief. Mark what qualifies as daruri.
Daruri here means self-evident and definitively proven, not merely rational.
2
Recognize the exception for doubt
Locate the phrases about 'quwwat al-shubhah' (strength of doubt) and 'ta'wil' (interpretation) preventing takfir.
The doubt must be strong, not whimsical.
3
Examine the Basmala example
Understand why denying the Qur'anicity of the Basmala is not automatically kufr: the inclusion is not daruri.
Because the Basmala's Qur'anicity is based on ahad reports, not tawatur.
4
Apply the Khawarij precedent
Analyze why Imam Ali (RA) did not declare the Khawarij disbelievers despite their rebellion, due to their (misguided) interpretation.
This shows the principle in action: strong doubt prevents takfir.
5
Conclude the rule
Formulate the final rule: denial of the daruri with interpretation, avoiding personal desire, is not kufr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في نفسه ضرورياً فإنكاره يوجب الكفر، ولعل هذا غير واف، فإن منكري عدم قرآنية البسملة لم ينكروا كون غير المتواتر غير قرآن، وإنما أنكروا اندراجه تحته، ولم يكن هذا الاندراج من الضروريات الدينية، وقس عليها حال مقرىء القرآنية، ثم إنما يأتي هذا الجواب والسؤال لو أريد بالضرورة البديهة ولو أريد القطيعة لسقط قول هذا القائل عن أصله كما لا يخفى على المتأمل (والجواب) أنه قد خفى التواتر فيه وقوى الشبهة حتى أدّى إلى الإشكال قبل التوغل في النظر، و(قوة الشبهة المؤدية إلى حد الإشكال مانع من التكفير لأن صاحبها يعد معذوراً) لأنه متأوّل والحاصل أن إنكار الضروري المقطوع بالتأويل مجانباً عن هوى النفس ليس كفراً، ولذا لم يكفر أمير المؤمنين رضي الله عنه الخوارج، حتى لم يمنع عن الصلاة معهم كما رواه الإمام محمد فافهم.
In itself essential, so denying it necessitates disbelief. But perhaps this is insufficient, for those who deny the Qur'anicity of the Basmala did not deny that non-mutawatir is not Qur'an; rather they denied its inclusion under [the definition of Qur'an], and this inclusion was not among the religious necessities. And analogize to it the case of the Qur'an reciter. Then this answer and question arise only if 'necessary' means self-evident. And if 'definitive' were intended, then this speaker's statement falls from its basis, as is not hidden from the reflective. (The answer): That tawatur was hidden in it and the doubt was strong until it led to confusion before deep investigation. And (the strength of the doubt leading to the limit of confusion prevents takfir because its holder is considered excused) because he is interpreting. The conclusion: Denial of the necessary definitive with interpretation, avoiding personal desire, is not disbelief. Hence the Commander of the Faithful, may Allah be pleased with him, did not declare the Khawarij disbelievers, to the extent that he did not forbid prayer with them, as narrated by Imam Muhammad. So understand.
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage discusses a nuanced usul rule: when does denial of a religious matter constitute kufr (disbelief)? The author clarifies that if a matter is 'daruri' (self-evident and definitively known), denying it is kufr. However, denying something that is not definitively established as part of the religion—like the Qur'anicity of the Basmala according to some—does not automatically make one a kafir, especially if there is a valid interpretative doubt. The example given is that Imam Ali (RA) did not declare the Khawarij disbelievers, despite their grave errors, because they had a (misguided) interpretation. Thus, strength of doubt (shubha) can prevent takfir. This is a key principle in Hanafi usul: takfir is avoided where interpretation is plausible.

Key Terms
ضروري (daruri): That which is self-evidently known and whose denial entails kufr
تواتر (tawatur): Uninterrupted transmission from generation to generation yielding certainty

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did Imam Ali (RA) not declare the Khawarij disbelievers according to the passage?
A) Because they were Muslims
B) Because their doubt was strong and they had an interpretation
C) Because they repented
D) Because they were too powerful

Key Takeaway
Denial of a daruri matter is kufr, but strong doubt and valid interpretation excuse the denier from takfir.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
beginner
6 min
Delaying the Communication of a Ruling to the Time of Need
Statement of the Hanafi position on delaying the delivery of a ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on delaying the communication of a ruling, identify its rational proof, and distinguish it from the minority view.

Core Idea
A ruling can be delayed until acted upon — no impossibility follows.

This lesson tackles a foundational usul principle: when must a Sharia ruling be communicated to those bound by it? The chosen Hanafi view allows the Lawgiver to postpone notifying the mukallaf until the moment of action, as long as no legal or rational harm results. This principle helps explain the gradual revelation of rulings and the absence of immediate obligation to know every rule in advance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Locate the exact statement of the Hanafi chosen position: delaying communication is permissible until the time of need.
The text says 'المختار جواز تأخير تبليغ الحكم المنزل إلى المكلف إلى وقت الحاجة'.
2
Identify the time of need
Define 'waqt al-haja' as the time when the ruling must be performed – whether the obligation has a broad or narrow window.
The text explains: 'وهو وقت تنجيز التكليف سواء كان موسعاً أو مضيقاً'.
3
Understand the exceptions
Note that delaying beyond the time of need is unanimously prohibited. Also note the minority view that even delaying until the time of need is not allowed.
The minority 'شرذمة قليلة' is mentioned, but the text sides with the majority.
4
Examine the rational proof
The proof is aqli (rational): no legal or rational impossibility (محال شرعي ولا عقلي) follows from delaying communication, so denial is obstinacy.
This is a straightforward rational argument, not dependent on a revealed text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة
الدلالة)
المختار جواز تأخير تبليغ الحكم المنزل إلى المكلف إلى وقت الحاجة) وهو وقت تنجيز التكليف سواء كان موسعاً أو مضيقاً، وقال شرذمة قليلة : لا يجوز، وأما التأخير عن وقت الحاجة فلا يجوز اتفاقاً لنا : لا يلزم منه (محال شرعي ولا عقلي، وإنكاره مكابرة (ولعل
Issue: (Indication) The chosen position is the permissibility of delaying the communication of the revealed ruling to the mukallaf until the time of need, which is the time of executing the obligation, whether it is broad or narrow. A small minority said: it is not permissible. As for delaying beyond the time of need, it is unanimously not permissible. For us: no legal or rational impossibility follows from it; denying it is obstinacy. Perhaps...
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage states a key usul principle: it is permissible for the Lawgiver to delay informing a legally responsible person (mukallaf) of a ruling until the time when that ruling needs to be acted upon. This applies whether the ruling has a broad time window (musa') or a narrow one (mudayyaq). A small minority rejected this, but the Hanafi (chosen) position is that there is no legal or rational objection. However, delaying beyond the time of need is unanimously prohibited. The proof is purely rational: no impossibility arises from such delay. This principle is foundational for understanding how rulings are communicated over time.

Key Terms
حكم (hukm): A Sharia ruling
مكلف (mukallaf): A legally responsible person
وقت الحاجة (waqt al-haja): The time when the ruling is to be acted upon
محال شرعي ولا عقلي (muhal shar'i wa la aqli): No legal or rational impossibility

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Is it permissible to delay informing a person of a ruling until the time of action?
A) Yes
B) No
C) Only for certain rulings
D) Only if the ruling is time-sensitive

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits delaying the communication of a revealed ruling to the time of need, based on the rational proof that no legal or rational impossibility follows from such delay.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
advanced
6 min
Permissibility of Delaying Proclamation of Ruling to Time of Need
Affirms the majority view that tabligh may be delayed to the time of need.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyse the Hanafi position on delaying tabligh and evaluate the argument that the command 'balligh' in 5:67 does not require immediate proclamation.

Core Idea
The command to proclaim does not demand immediacy; delay until needed is permissible.

This passage addresses a key usul question: When a ruling is revealed, must the Prophet convey it immediately? The Hanafi school, representing the majority, holds that delaying proclamation until the time of need is permissible. A small minority argues that the command 'balligh' in Surah al-Ma'idah implies immediacy. We will examine the evidence from both sides, focusing on the linguistic analysis of the verse and the concept of fawr (immediacy) vs. tarakhi (delay).

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the two positions
First, clearly state the issue: Is it permissible to delay the proclamation (tabligh) of a revealed ruling to the time of need? The chosen (mukhtar) view of the Hanafis is yes; a small group says no. Delaying beyond need is unanimously prohibited.
The time of need (waqt al-haja) is when the obligation becomes due, whether broad (like Zuhr time) or narrow.
2
Examine the opponent's dalil
The minority cites Surah al-Ma'idah (5:67): 'O Messenger, proclaim what has been revealed to you.' They argue that the imperative (amr) implies immediacy (fawr). Additionally, they claim that the obligation of tabligh is known rationally from prophethood, so textual evidence is unnecessary if delay is allowed.
The opponent's second point attempts to show that if delay were permissible, the verse would be redundant.
3
Analyse the Hanafi rebuttal
The Hanafis reject the claim of fawr. They point to the continuation of the verse: 'And if you do not do so, then you have not conveyed His message.' This conditional shows that failure to act immediately does not mean the message was not conveyed. Therefore, the command is not for fawr. As for the rational knowledge, the textual elucidation serves to strengthen (taqwiya) the intellect, not to establish the obligation from scratch.
The commentary in 'al-Tahrir' notes that the verse may specifically refer to the Quran itself (al-matlu), but the Hanafis argue that the word 'ma' is general.
4
Evaluate the deeper linguistic point
The passage discusses whether the verse is general (amm) or specific to the Quran. Some narrations indicate that some revelations are secrets not to be proclaimed to all. The Hanafis maintain that the verse is general unless there is evidence for specification, and the existence of secrets does not negate the general obligation of tabligh to those who are qualified.
This touches on the usul principle: al-amm yujra ala umumihi hatta yarida dalil al-takhsis.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Consider a modern scenario: A religious authority receives a new revelation (hypothetically) or ruling. According to the Hanafi view, they may delay announcing it until the time when people actually need to act upon it, provided they do not delay beyond that time. This contrasts with the view that immediate announcement is required.
This application shows the practical consequence of the ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة
المختار جواز تأخير تبليغ الحكم المنزل إلى المكلف إلى وقت الحاجة وهو وقت تنجيز التكليف سواء كان موسعاً أو مضيقاً، وقال شرذمة قليلة : لا يجوز، وأما التأخير عن وقت الحاجة فلا يجوز اتفاقاً. لنا : لا يلزم منه محال شرعي ولا عقلي، وإنكاره مكابرة. ولعل فيه مصلحة يطلع عليها رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم، فيجب التأخير حينئذ. المنكرون (قالوا) قال الله تعالى: ﴿ يَآ أَيُّهَا الرَّسُولُ بَلِّغْ مَا أُنزِلَ إِلَيْكَ ﴾ [المائدة: ٦٧] والأمر ههنا للفور. و إلا فوجوب التبليغ مطلقاً سواء كان على الفور أو متراخياً معلوم عقلاً من الرسالة فلا حاجة إلى الإبانة. (قلنا) لا نسلم أنه للفور، وأما إبانة التبليغ مع كونه معلوماً عقلاً فلأنها لفائدة، وفائدته تقوية العقل أي تقوية ما حكم به العقل بالنقل. أقول : يدل على ذلك أي عدم كونه للفور ما بعده هو قوله تعالى: ﴿ وَإِن لَّمْ تَفْعَلْ فَمَا بَلَّغْتَ رِسَالَتَهُ ﴾ [المائدة: ٦٧] فإن عدم فعل التبليغ على الفور لا يوجب عدم تبليغ الرسالة رأساً، وهذا ظاهر، إلا أن يتحمل التكلف ويقال : لما كان وجوب التبليغ الفوري عندهم فتركه ترك التبليغ المستحق الذي هو الرسالة فتدبر. وقد يجاب في «التحرير» بأنه ظاهر في تبليغ المتلو وهو القرآن الشريف، فلا يلزم منه إلا عدم جواز تأخير تبليغه لا عدم جواز تأخير التبليغ مطلقاً، والمدعي هذا دون ذلك وفيه ما فيه فإن كلمة ما عامة والتخصيص من غير دليل على أنه نزل في تبليغ حكم غير متلو كما ورد في بعض الروايات ولا يتوهم أنها ليست على عمومها، فإن بعض ما أنزل أسرار بين الله ورسوله صلوات الله عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه فلا يصح التبليغ، لأن الآية ظاهرة في العموم، فلا تسمع دعوى أن بعض ما أنزل أسرار ممنوع التبليغ إلا عن البعض الغير المتأهلين وهو لا ينافي وجوب التبليغ مطلقاً فافهم .
Issue: The chosen (view) is the permissibility of delaying the proclamation of the revealed ruling to the accountable person until the time of need, which is the time of actual obligation, whether the obligation is broad (musa') or narrow (mudayyaq). And a small handful said: It is not permissible. As for delaying beyond the time of need, it is impermissible by agreement. For us: It does not necessitate any impossibility in Shari'a or reason, and its denial is obstinacy. Perhaps there is a benefit known to the Messenger of Allah (peace and blessings be upon him and his family) that necessitates delaying at that time. The deniers said: Allah said: 'O Messenger, proclaim what has been revealed to you' (5:67). The command here is for immediacy (fawr). Otherwise, the obligation of proclamation in absolute terms, whether immediate or delayed, is known rationally from the office of prophethood, so there is no need for textual elucidation. We say: We do not accept that it is for immediacy. As for the elucidation of proclamation even though it is rationally known, it is for a benefit, and its benefit is to strengthen the intellect, i.e., to strengthen what the intellect has judged by transmission. I say: That which indicates this, i.e., that it is not for immediacy, is what follows it, namely His statement: 'And if you do not do so, then you have not conveyed His message' (5:67). For failure to act immediately does not entail not conveying the message at all. This is apparent, unless one resorts to affectation and says: Since the obligation of immediate proclamation according to them, then abandoning it is abandoning the due proclamation which is the message. So reflect. And it is answered in 'al-Tahrir' that it is apparent regarding the proclamation of the recited text (al-matlu), i.e., the noble Quran, so nothing follows from it except the impermissibility of delaying its proclamation, not the impermissibility of delaying proclamation absolutely. And the claimant claims this without that, and it has its problems. For the word 'ma' is general, and specification without evidence that it was revealed regarding the proclamation of a non-recited ruling, as reported in some narrations, is not effective. And one should not imagine that it is not general. For some of what has been revealed are secrets between Allah and His Messenger (peace and blessings be upon him and his family), so proclamation is not valid. Because the verse is apparent in generality, so the claim that some of what has been revealed are secrets prohibited from proclamation except to some who are not qualified is not entertained. And this does not contradict the obligation of proclamation absolutely. So understand.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage discusses the permissibility of delaying the proclamation (tabligh) of a revealed ruling to the accountable person until the time of need. The majority (mukhtar) holds that it is permissible to delay until the time of obligation, whether the obligation is broad (like prayer during its time) or narrow (like an immediate obligation). A small group (shurdhama qalila) says it is not permissible. Delaying beyond the time of need is unanimously impermissible. The Hanafi evidence is that no impossibility (muhal) arises from such delay, and rejecting it is obstinacy. Furthermore, there may be wisdom (maslaha) known to the Prophet that necessitates delay. The opponents cite the Quranic verse 'O Messenger, proclaim what has been revealed to you' (5:67), arguing that the command is for immediate action (fawr). The Hanafis respond by pointing to the immediate continuation of the verse: 'And if you do not do so, then you have not conveyed His message.' This shows that failing to act immediately does not mean the message was not conveyed, since the consequence is only for complete non-proclamation. Thus, the command is not for fawr. The passage also notes that the command in the verse may specifically refer to the Quran itself (al-matlu), not to all rulings. However, the Hanafis argue that the word 'ma' is general, and specification without evidence is invalid. Some revelations are secrets between Allah and the Prophet, so they are not to be proclaimed to everyone; this does not negate the general obligation of proclamation to those who are qualified.

Key Terms
تأخير تبليغ الحكم (ta'khir tabligh al-hukm): Delaying the proclamation of a revealed ruling to the accountable person beyond the time of revelation but before the time of need.
وقت الحاجة (waqt al-haja): The time of need, i.e., the time when the obligation is actually to be performed (time of tangible obligation). It can be broad (musa') like the entire time of Zuhr prayer, or narrow (mudayyaq) like a specific moment for an expiation.
الفور (al-fawr): Immediacy. The view that a command requires instant compliance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position presented in the passage, what is the ruling on delaying the proclamation of a revealed ruling beyond the time of need?
A) It is permissible as long as there is a beneficial purpose.
B) It is impermissible by agreement (ittiqaqan).
C) It is permissible only if the ruling is from the Quran, not Sunnah.
D) It is always permissible regardless of time.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits delaying tabligh until the time of need because the Quranic command does not imply immediacy, and there may be benefit in delay.

12 min
Khabar vs Insha': The Hanafi Argument for Performative Divorce Utterances
Analyzing linguistic nature of divorce/sale utterances to prove they are insha'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the linguistic categories of khabar and insha' and apply the Hanafi argument to conclude that divorce/sale utterances are insha' rather than khabar.

Core Idea
Divorce utterances create the divorce; they do not report a prior divorce.

In this lesson, we examine a foundational distinction in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: whether utterances like 'You are divorced' are reports (khabar) or performatives (insha'). The text from Fawatih al-Rahamut argues forcefully for the latter, using logical reasoning and observed practice. Understanding this distinction is crucial for grasping how legal effects are created through speech in Hanafi law.

Guided Path
1
Understand the khabar/insha' distinction
Define khabar (speech that can be true or false, reporting an external fact) and insha' (speech that creates a new reality). Note the implications for truth-value.
Khabar is truth-apt; insha' is not.
2
Examine the challenge: could divorce utterances be khabar?
Consider the counterargument that 'You are divorced' reports the husband's mental intention to divorce or the woman's already-existing divorced status.
This is the view the passage refutes.
3
Analyze the absurd consequence
If it were khabar, the divorce would need to exist before the utterance, leading to a logical contradiction—divorce occurs by the utterance, not before.
The passage highlights this as 'ظاهر الفساد' (clearly corrupt).
4
Trace the Hanafi rebuttal
The utterance is a legal cause (sabab) conditioned on intention, not a report. The mental construction (insha' nafsi) becomes effective only at the moment of utterance, as signified by the utterance itself.
The analogy with travel and hardship illustrates this: the ruling is attached to the utterance as a sign, not to the underlying mental state.
5
Evaluate the supporting proof
The observed fact that divorce and sale occur upon uttering these formulae is the evidence. If they were khabar, no legal effect would follow.
This is the 'dalil' from observed practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اتصاف اللفظ والإخبار عن حدوث البيع من الكلام النفسي والتغاير بين الحكاية والمحكي عنه بالاعتبار، فالمحكي عنه هو إحداث البيع القائم بالنفس والحكاية هو من حيث إنه مدلول اللفظ مطابقة، وأنت لا يذهب عليك أن هذا مع ابتنائه على التغاير الاعتباري لا يفيد لأن المستدل إنما ألزم عدم الفرق بين ما إذا قصد الحكاية عن طلاق واقع أو بيع واقع، وبين ما إذا قصد حدوث آخر لكونه إخباراً على كل حال هذا لا يدفع ذلك، وبيان الفرق بينه حال كونه إنشاء وبينه حال كونه إخباراً مما لا طائل والقطع بالفرق في الحكاية عن الخارج لا يضره، بل يفيد بطلان اللازم فلا وجه له إلا بالإرجاع إلى ما قال المصنف (وقد يقال) في الجواب : (الفرق بينه خبراً وبينه إنشاء إنه إخبار عن (الذهن أي عن الإنشاء القائم بالذهن (مرة) فيقع آخر (وأخرى عن الخارج أي عن الطلاق الواقع في الخارج وفيه ما فيه) فإنك قد عرفت أن السبب الموجب لوقوع الطلاق هو الإنشاء القائم بالنفس وبه تصير المرأة مطلقة في الخارج، والرجل بائعاً والمال مبيعاً، فنحو طلقتك وأنت طالق حكاية عن هذا الإنشاء الذهني أو الأثر المرتب عليه فلا وجه لهذا الفرق ؛ نعم : قد يكون إخباراً عن الإنشاء الأول الذي به وقع الطلاق مرة، وحكى عنه أولاً وعلم وجوده بهذه الحكاية فلا يقع طلاق آخر، وقد يكون إخباراً عن إنشاء ذهني آخر غير الأول . فيقع آخر، ولذا يسأل في الرجعي كما قد مر، وقد يقال في الاستدلال على الإنشائية بأن : أنت طالق وطلقتك لو كانا خبرين كان الأول خبراً عن المرأة بالطلاق والثاني عن اتصاف الزوج بالتطليق، فهذا المخبر عنه ثابت من قبل أم لا . وعلى الثاني فلا إخبار، بل يكون إنشاء لتطليق الزوج وصيرورة المرأة متصفة به فإنهما قد تحققا بهذا، وعلى الأول يلزم أن تكون المرأة مطلقة قبل هذا الكلام وهو ظاهر الفساد لأن الطلاق إنما يقع به لا قبل، والقول بنوط الحكم بهذا اللفظ كما في السفر والشقة لا يفيد، لأن الشارع قد أناط الحكم على السفر ولم يعتبر المشقة فيه أصلاً إنما هو إبداء للحكمة منا، وأما ههنا فقد قلتم إن إيقاع الطلاق قد أناطه الشرع بعقد القلب، وإنما هذا حكاية وإخبار عنه لا دخل له في الإيقاع، وأيضاً لا بد لهذه الإناطة من دليل شرعي لأنه لا يهتدي إليه العقل، ولا يجوز نصب الأسباب بالرأي وأيضاً : لا يكون حينئذ هذا من قبيل المقتضى فإنه يثبت بالمقتضى، وهذا ما ثبت من قبل، والجواب عنه : أن المخبر عنه ثابت قبل التكلم بهذه الأخبار، وأن المرأة مطلقة قبله بالإنشاء النفسي، وليس فيه فساد أصلاً، وإناطة الحكم على هذا اللفظ مع كونه إخباراً لغة لأنه اعتبر سببية الإنشاء النفسي لئلا يلزم اعتبار الكلام الكاذب ومعنى نوط الحكم بهذه الصيغ أن العقد النفسي المخبر عنه إنما جعل سبباً شرعاً عند هذا الإخبار مقدماً عليه، فيكون ظهور سببيته بهذه الأخبار، ويكون الوقوع أيضاً عنده والدليل عليه وقوع الطلاق والبيع عند استعمال هذه الصيغ، وهذا هو الدليل على أن الحال حال السفر والمشقة، ثم لما كان اعتبار سببية هذا المعنى النفسي لوقوع الطلاق وصيرورة المرأة مطلقة إنما هو مشروط بإرادة الحكاية لإناطة الشارع الحكم بهذه الألفاظ لا على النفسي كيف اتفق كما أن إناطة الرخصة بالسفر دلت على أنه لا اعتبار للمشقة كيفما اتفقت بل حال كونها مقارنة للسفر وكان سببية هذا الإنشاء النفسي لوقوع الطلاق إنما تظهر بهذا الإخبار قيل : إنها ثابتة باقتضائه، وإن هذه الألفاظ أسباب لأحكامها لكونها مظنة لها، وهذا كلام صافٍ لا غبار عليه قد تفضل الله سبحانه بالكشف على هذا العبد غفر الله له إلى هذا الآن ولعله يحدث بعد ذلك أمراً
The description of the word and the information about the occurrence of sale from internal speech and the distinction between the report (hikaya) and the reported (mahki 'anhu) by consideration, so the reported is the bringing into existence of sale subsisting in the soul, and the report is in terms of it being the meaning of the word by correspondence. And you are not unaware that this, being based on notional distinction, does not benefit, because the arguer only necessitated the lack of difference between when one intends to report about an actual divorce or an actual sale, and when one intends another occurrence, because it is informative in all cases; this does not repel that. And explaining the difference between it in the state of being construction (insha') and in the state of being informative (khabar) is of no use, and the categorical difference in reporting about the external does not harm it; rather it benefits the invalidity of the necessary consequence, so there is no way except to refer to what the author said: 'It may be said in answer: the difference between it as informative and it as construction is that it is information about the mind, i.e., about the construction subsisting in the mind, once, so another occurs; and another time about the external, i.e., about the divorce occurring in the external, and in it is what is in it.' For you have known that the cause necessitating the occurrence of divorce is the construction subsisting in the soul, and by it the woman becomes divorced in the external, and the man a seller, and the property sold. So expressions like 'I divorce you' and 'You are divorced' are a report about this mental construction or the effect dependent on it, so there is no basis for this difference. Yes: it may be informative about the first construction by which the divorce occurred once, and it has been reported about it and its existence is known by this report, so no other divorce occurs; and it may be informative about another mental construction other than the first, so another occurs. For this reason, one is asked about the revocable (raj'i) as has passed. And it may be said in argument for being construction (insha'iyya) that: 'You are divorced' and 'I divorce you' if they were informative, the first would be information about the woman being divorced, and the second about the husband's being characterized with divorcing. So this reported thing is established beforehand or not? On the second, there is no information, rather it is a construction of the husband's divorcing and the woman's becoming characterized with it, for they have both been actualized by this. On the first, it would necessitate that the woman was divorced before this speech, which is clearly corrupt, because divorce only occurs by it, not before. And the saying of attaching the ruling to this word, like in travel and hardship, does not benefit, because the Lawgiver has attached the ruling to travel and did not consider hardship in it at all; rather it is a display of wisdom from us. But here, you have said that the Lawgiver has attached the occurrence of divorce to the heart's contract, and this is only a report and information about it, having no role in the occurrence. Also, this attachment must have a textual proof, because reason cannot guide to it, and it is not permissible to establish causes by opinion. Also, then this would not be of the type of mūjib (requirer), for it is established by the mūjib, and this was not established beforehand. The answer to it is that the reported thing is established before speaking these reports, and the woman is divorced before it by the mental construction, and there is no corruption in it at all. The attachment of the ruling to this word despite it being informative linguistically is because he considered the causality of the mental construction, to avoid considering false speech. And the meaning of attaching the ruling to these formulae is that the mental contract which is reported about is made a legal cause at the time of this report, precedence given to it, so its causality appears by these reports, and the occurrence also occurs at it. The evidence for it is the occurrence of divorce and sale when these formulae are used, and this is the evidence that the case is like the case of travel and hardship. Then, since the consideration of the causality of this mental meaning for the occurrence of divorce and the woman becoming divorced is conditional on intending the report, because of the Lawgiver's attachment of the ruling to these words, not to the mental meaning in any case, just as the attachment of the license to travel indicated that hardship is not considered in any case but only in the state of being concomitant with travel. And the causality of this mental construction for the occurrence of divorce only appears by this report. It is said: it is established by its requirement (iqtida'), and these words are causes for their rulings because they are the locus (mazannah) for them. This is clear speech with no dust on it. Allah the Glorious has favored this servant (may Allah forgive him) with disclosure until now, and perhaps after that an event will occur.
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage is a detailed analysis of the distinction between khabar (informative) and insha' (performative/constructive) speech, focusing on utterances like 'You are divorced' and 'I divorce you'. The author argues that these are insha' because they create the legal effect (divorce, sale) rather than reporting a prior fact. The discussion counters the view that they could be khabar, which would absurdly imply the woman was already divorced before the utterance. The author also addresses the counterargument that the mental construction (insha' nafsi) is the real cause, and the utterance merely reports it, but the response is that the causality of the mental construction is conditioned on the utterance, as evidenced by the fact that divorce occurs upon the utterance. The passage uses an analogy with travel and hardship to show that the ruling is attached to the utterance as a sign, not to the underlying mental state. The evidence offered is the observed occurrence of divorce and sale upon using these formulae.

Key Terms
خبر (khabar): Speech that reports something external and can be true or false.
إنشاء (insha'): Speech that brings about a change in the external world without reporting a pre-existing fact.
حكاية (hikaya): A report or narrative about something, often used interchangeably with khabar.
إنشاء نفسي (insha' nafsi): The mental construction or intention that is the real cause of the legal effect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi analysis in the passage, why does uttering 'I divorce you' (طلقتك) not count as a report (khabar)?
A) Because it would require the woman to be already divorced, leading to absurdity.
B) Because it is a lie according to the Lawgiver.
C) Because it is only a report of the mental construction, which is the real cause.
D) Because it is a performative utterance that creates the divorce.

Key Takeaway
Divorce and sale utterances are insha' (performatives) that create legal effects at the moment of utterance, not reports of prior facts.

Hanafi Classification of the Locus of Khabar Wahid
Hanafi classification of khabar wahid by legal domain

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify legal matters into rights of Allah and rights of servants, and apply the corresponding conditions for accepting khabar wahid in each category.

Core Idea
Hanafis divide legal matters into huquq Allah and huquq al-'ibad, applying different standards for accepting solitary reports based on presence of compulsion.

This passage sets out the Hanafi framework for determining when a solitary report (khabar wahid) is legally acceptable. Rather than applying a single standard, the Hanafis differentiate based on the nature of the matter—whether it pertains to the rights of Allah (huquq Allah) or the rights of servants (huquq al-'ibad), and within the latter, whether the matter involves pure compulsion (ilzam mahd), no compulsion, or mixed compulsion. Understanding this classification is essential for correctly applying hadith reports in legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main categories
First, note that the Hanafis divide all legal matters into two broad categories: the rights of Allah (huquq Allah) and the rights of servants (huquq al-'ibad). Huquq Allah include punishments (hudud) and acts of worship/transactions (ibadat/mu'amalat). Huquq al-'ibad include personal dealings and claims.
The classification is hierarchical; each category has its own rules for accepting reports.
2
Analyze huquq Allah
For huquq Allah, a report from a single just narrator ('adl) is accepted in both punishments and worship/transactions (e.g., informing about purity/impurity of water). However, a report from a fasiq (sinner) is not accepted; in such cases, one must perform taharri (search for the truth) and act accordingly.
The passage mentions that if a fasiq reports impurity, one must do taharri; if it leads to impurity, tayammum is performed, and pouring out the water beforehand is recommended.
3
Subdivide huquq al-'ibad
Huquq al-'ibad are further subdivided into three: (a) matters involving pure compulsion (ilzam mahd) like sales when one party denies, (b) matters with no compulsion at all like gifts and agencies, and (c) matters with compulsion in one aspect but not another.
The passage focuses on (a) and (b); (c) is implied but not elaborated.
4
Apply conditions for ilzam mahd
In ilzam mahd, additional conditions beyond those for riwaya are required: the reporter must have authority (wilaya) over the matter (e.g., cannot be a disbeliever testifying against a Muslim, nor a slave), must use the wording of shahada (ashhadu), and must meet number and gender requirements (two men or one man+two women).
An exception is the midwife's testimony: due to necessity, number and masculinity are not required, as men do not attend childbirth.
5
Apply conditions for matters with no compulsion
For matters without compulsion (e.g., reports about meat being from a Muslim or Kitabi slaughter), only tamyiz (discernment) is required. The reporter must be a discerning person (e.g., a discerning minor, not a child, insane, or mentally deficient), and his report is accepted if his heart is truthful (tasdiq al-qalb).
No requirement of number, gender, or lafz; sincerity and basic discernment suffice.

Source Text

تقسيم للحنفية (محل الخبر مطلقاً) من تقييد كونه خبراً عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم (إما حقوق الله تعالى وهي عقوبات أولاً كالعبادات والمعاملات وهو) أي خبر الواحد العدل (حجة فيهما ) أي العقوبات والعبادات كالإخبار بطهارة الماء ونجاسته، فإذا أخبر العدل بنجاسته يباح التيمم والإخبار عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم. فإن حكمها الوجوب وهو عبادة (كما مر ) ولا يقبل فيها خبر فاسق فلا يجوز التيمم بإخبار الفاسق بنجاسة الماء، بل يعمل بالتحري فإن وقع التحري على الطهور يتوضأ إن أخبر الفاسق بالنجاسة، وضم التيمم أحب، وإن وقع على النجاسة يتيمم وإراقة الماء قبله أحب (وإما حقوق العباد) فإما فيه إلزام ،محض ، أو ليس فيه إلزام أصلاً أو فيه من وجه دون وجه (فما فيه إلزام محض كالبيوع عند إنكار أحدهما (ونحوها) كدعاوى أخرى فيشترط مع شرائط الرواية الولاية فلا يقبل قول الكافر على المسلم، ولا قول العبد ولفظ الشهادة والعدد وكون المخبرين رجلين اثنين أو امرأتين مع رجل واحد عند الإمكان، فلا عدد ولا (ذكورة شرط (في شهادة القابلة) بالولادة، فإنه لا يحضر الرجل عندها فسقطت، وقد صح عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم أنه قبل شهادة القابلة ولا إسلام في الشهادة على الكافر) إذ قلما يشاهد المسلم معاملة الكفار، ففيه ضرورة أيضاً، وفيه خلاف الشافعي رحمه الله تعالى (وما لا إلزام فيه) أصلاً (كالوكالات والهدايا ونحوها ومنه أخبار كون اللحم الذي يباع في الأسواق ذبيحة مسلم أو كتابي فلا يشترط سوى التمييز فلا يقبل قول الصبي الغير المميز، والمعتوه غير المميز، والمجنون، ويقبل قول المميز (مع تصديق القلب) صدق المخبر، فإذا جاءت جارية وأخبرت
A division by the Hanafis: The locus of the report absolutely, restricted to it being a report from the Messenger of Allah, is either rights of Allah, which are punishments first, like acts of worship and transactions, and it (khabar wahid 'adl) is a proof in both — punishments and acts of worship, like informing about the purity or impurity of water. So if an 'adl informs of its impurity, tayammum is permitted... And if it is rights of servants, then either there is pure compulsion (ilzam mahd) like sales when one of them denies, etc. — then along with conditions of riwaya, authority (wilaya) is required, so the word of a disbeliever against a Muslim is not accepted, nor the word of a slave; and the wording of shahada and number are required... except in the testimony of a midwife, where number and masculinity are not conditions because men do not attend, and it is established that the Prophet accepted the testimony of a midwife... And what has no compulsion at all, like agencies, gifts, etc., includes reports that meat sold in markets is from a Muslim or Kitabi slaughter — then only discrimination (tamyiz) is required, so the word of a non-discerning child, insane person, or mentally deficient is not accepted, but the word of a discerning minor with truthfulness of heart is accepted.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed Hanafi classification of where khabar wahid is accepted. It divides matters into rights of Allah (huquq Allah), including punishments and worship/transactions, where khabar 'adl is accepted (but not from a fasiq, requiring taharrī), and rights of servants (huquq al-'ibad). The latter is further divided into three categories: (1) matters involving pure compulsion (ilzam mahd) like sales and claims, where stricter conditions apply: the reporter must have authority (wilaya), cannot be a disbeliever or slave, and must use the wording of shahada with number and gender requirements, except in necessity like the midwife's testimony; (2) matters with no compulsion (like gifts and reports about meat), requiring only tamyiz (discernment) and sincerity of heart; (3) matters with compulsion in one aspect but not another (implied). The passage illustrates the nuanced Hanafi approach to accepting reports based on the nature of the case.

Key Terms
حقوق الله (huquq Allah): Rights of Allah, including acts of worship and fixed punishments that are obligations owed to Him.
حقوق العباد (huquq al-'ibad): Rights of servants, involving transactions, claims, and personal dealings where individuals' interests are at stake.
إلزام محض (ilzam mahd): Pure compulsion; a legal situation where one party is forced to transfer property or accept a claim without choice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi classification in this passage, which of the following statements is correct regarding the acceptance of a report about the purity of water?
A) The report of a fasiq is accepted if the water is proven pure through other means.
B) The report of an 'adl is accepted; if a fasiq reports, one must perform taharri.
C) The report of any Muslim, whether 'adl or fasiq, is accepted for acts of worship.
D) The report requires two male witnesses even in huquq Allah.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school classifies legal matters into huquq Allah and huquq al-'ibad, and further subdivides the latter by presence of compulsion, each with distinctive conditions for accepting solitary reports.

Conditions of Tahammul and Ada' Regarding Age and Sanity
Explaining conditions for hadith narration: tamyiz for tahammul, bulugh and sanity for ada'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for tahammul and ada' in hadith narration according to the Hanafi school, and apply the analogy to testimony to derive the rulings.

Core Idea
Tamyiz suffices for receiving hadith, but bulugh and sanity are required for transmitting it.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahmut clarifies the legal conditions for hadith narration according to the Hanafi school. It distinguishes between tahammul (learning) and ada' (teaching), showing that the requirements differ: tamyiz (discernment) is enough for tahammul, while bulugh (puberty) and sanity are needed for ada'. The author supports this by analogy to testimony (shahada) and by the practice of the Companions who accepted narrations from minors. The passage also addresses counterarguments and the status of the near-adult (murahiq).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two acts and their conditions
Read the Arabic passage carefully to extract the conditions for tahammul (تحمل) and ada' (أداء). Note that tamyiz is the condition for tahammul, while bulugh and sanity are conditions for ada'.
Look for the phrase: 'فإن شرط التحمل التمييز وشرط الأداء البلوغ والسلامة من الجنون' (paraphrased).
2
Understand the rationale
Why is tamyiz sufficient for tahammul but not for ada'? The author explains that ada' is like testifying (shahada), which requires full accountability (taklif). A child can learn with basic understanding, but transmission requires reliability.
The qiyas (analogy) to shahada is key: 'قياساً على الشهادة'.
3
Examine the textual evidence
Identify the proof texts used: the practice of the Companions (Ibn Abbas, Ibn al-Zubayr, Nu'man ibn Bashir, Anas) who narrated from before bulugh, and the qiyas on shahada.
The dalil naqli is the acceptance of their narrations without questioning their age at tahammul.
4
Analyze the counterarguments
The passage addresses objections: (1) that making children listen implies acceptance – rejected because it could be for blessing. (2) The murahiq (near-adult) – some accept with investigation, but the Hanafi position rejects due to lack of taklif.
The text refutes the Quba' incident by showing the informant was not the minor.
5
Distinguish the Hanafi position
Synthesize the Hanafi rule: tahammul is valid with tamyiz from any age; ada' is valid only after bulugh and sanity, even if the narration was heard earlier.
This contrasts with views that accept murahiq or set a minimum age for tahammul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باختلاف الصبيان (بل) التقدير (بفهم الخطاب ورد الجواب فإذا كان الصبي بحيث يفهم الخطاب، ويرد الجواب يكون صالحاً لتحمل الحديث، لكن في الغالب لا يكون على هذه الحيثية قبل بلوغ السبعة ولذا أمر الأولياء بأمرهم بالصلاة حين بلوغهم هذا السن، وأما تعقل محمود بن الربيع سنة خمس أو أربع وحفظ الإمام الشافعي الموطأ» وهو ابن خمس وحفظ الإمام سهل بن عبد الله التستري بعض الأوراد وهو ابن سنتين، فمن جملة الكرامات لا يبنى عليه الأمر في الغالب. نعم : لو وجد على هذه الصفات تحمله البتة، ولذا ما شرطنا صح سناً، لكنه قلما يوجد فافهم . (و) الشرط (للأداء الكمال للعقل، وهو أيضاً مختلف باختلاف الرجال، فلا يمكن تعيين قدر منه فأدير سببه مقامه شرعاً، كما في السفر والمشقة، قال (ومعياره البلوغ سالماً) عن العته والجنون وإنما شرطنا نفس التمييز للتحمل وكماله للأداء (قياساً على الشهادة) لكونهما إخبارين (و لقبولهم) عبد الله بن عباس و) عبد الله بن الزبير والنعمان بن بشير (وأنس بن مالك رواياتهم بلا استفسار منهم أنهم تحملوا قبل البلوغ أو بعده، فعلم أن البلوغ ليس شرطاً عند التحمل وأما اشتراطه عند الأداء فيجيء وجهه.
واعلم أن عبد الله بن عباس ولد لثلاث سنين قبل الهجرة في قول الواقدي، فعمره حين وفاته له ثلاث عشرة سنة ، كذا في «الاستيعاب». وقال ابن عبد البر فيه : وقد روينا من وجوه عن سعيد بن جبير عن ابن عباس : توفي رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم وأنا ابن عشر سنين، وقد قرأت المحكم، يعني المفصل . ثم روي بإسناد آخر من طريق عبد الله عن أبيه بإسناده عن ابن عباس : توفي رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم وأنا ابن خمس عشرة سنة، وقد روى البخاري أنه ناهز الاحتلام في أيام حجة الوداع، فحينئذ لا يتحقق بلوغه عند التحمل أصلاً، وكذا عبد الله بن الزبير أول مولود في الإسلام بعد الهجرة بسنة أو سنتين في المشهور وقيل في الأولى، فجميع مسموعاته كانت قبل البلوغ، فإن مدة إقامته عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه الصلاة والسلام بالمدينة عشر سنين، وكذا النعمان بن بشير أول مولود في الأنصار بعد الهجرة، وتوفي رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وهو ابن ثمان سنين، وقيل: ست سنين قال ابن عبد البر في الاستيعاب : والأول أصح إن شاء الله، لأن الأكثر يقولون : إنه بن الزبير ولدا لسنتين من الهجرة وروى الطبري أن ابن الزبير قال : النعمان بن بشير أسن مني بستة أشهر، فجميع مسموعاته أيضاً قبل البلوغ وأما أنس بن مالك فكان ابن عشر سنين حين قدم رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم وابن عشرين حين توفي، فكان أكثر مسموعاته قبل البلوغ، وقد قبلوه كله وأما ما روى ابن عبد البر أنه شهد بدراً فما كان شهوده للقتال بل لخدمة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم، فإنه كان خادماً له رضي الله عنه، فقد بان لك أن الأوجه في الاستدلال أن يقال : لأنهم مسموعاتهم رضوان الله عليهم قبل البلوغ فافهم. وقد استدل بأنه جرت عادة السلف بإسماع الصبيان، فلو لم تقبل مسموعاتهم لما كان له فائدة ولم يرتض به المص ( و ) قال (أما الإسماع للصبيان فغير مستلزم) للمطلوب لاحتمال التبرك والاعتياد بالرواية وهما من أعظم الفوائد (وقيل: المراهق مقبول)
رواية وأداء، لكن لا مطلقاً بل ( مع التحري) فإن وقع على الصدق يقبل وإلا لا (و) قال في «التحرير» لإبطاله المعتمد في هذا الباب الصحابة، ولم يرجعوا إليه) أي المراهق فهو غير مقبول (أقول غاية ما لزم منه فقدان الدليل، ولا يلزم من انتفاء الدليل انتفاء المدلول) وهو غير واضح، فإنه يستدل بانتفاء المراجعة على عدم قبوله فعدم الرجوع دليل عليه فالأحرى يقال : لعل عدم المراجعة لعدم حاجتهم إلى المراجعة إليهم فلا يصلح حجة (بل الوجه) في (إبطاله) تهمة عدم التكليف فإن المراهق غير مكلف، فلا الكذب عليه، فيجوز أن يحرموه وهو إذ ذاك يكذب، فلهذه التهمة لا يقبل كما في الفاسق بل أولى قال من يقبل المراهق أن أهل قباء قبلوا أنس مالك وابن عمر وهما إذ ذاك غير بالغين فأجاب بقوله : (واعتماد أهل قباء على بن أنس أو ابن عمر بسن البلوغ على الأصح) وقد عرفت أن أنساً كان يوم القدوم الشريف ابن عشر، وكان تحول القبلة بعده بستة عشر شهراً أو سبعة عشر كما في «صحيح البخاري»، فكيف يكون بالغاً؟ وأما ابن عمر ففي الاستيعاب : قال الواقدي : كان يوم بدر ممن لم يحتلم، فاستصغره رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم ،ورده، فكيف يكون بالغاً عند تحول القبلة، وأعجب من هذا ما قيل إن الصحيح أن المخبر أنس وابن عمر معاً، بالغ وأسن من ابن عمر وقبلوا قوله فإنه قد بان لك أن الأمر بالعكس، فالحق في الجواب أن أنساً وابن عمر راويان والمخبر غيرهما، فإنه في رواية أنس : فمر رجل من بني سلمة وهم ركوع في صلاة الفجر، وفي رواية ابن عمر بينما الناس بقباء بصلاة الصبح إذ جاءهم آت إلى الآخر، فقيل: هو عباد بن بشر في التيسير»، قال الحافظ العسقلاني : إنه أرجح رواه ابن خيثمة، وفي «التحرير»: هو عباد بن نهيك عند المحدثين، وهو شيخ كبير، وعباد بن بشر قتل شهيداً اليمامة وهو ابن خمس وأربعين سنة ونهيك ككريم والذي يظهر لهذا العبد أنه يوم المخبر لأهل مسجد بني حارثة لا لأهل مسجد قباء والله أعلم . ثم لو سلم أن المخبر إياهم أنس أو ابن عمر فغاية ما لزم قبول أهل قباء، هو ليس حجة، فإن تشبث بتقرير النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فممنوع، بل قال هم آمنوا بالغيب فلم يعد هذا الخبر خبراً فافهم.
With the difference of children, the estimate is (by understanding the address and returning the answer). So when the child is such that he understands the address and returns the answer, he becomes fit for carrying (tahammul) of hadith. But mostly he does not have this condition before the age of seven, therefore guardians are commanded to order them to pray upon reaching this age. As for the intellectual grasp of Mahmud ibn al-Rabi' at five or four years, and Imam al-Shafi'i memorizing al-Muwatta' at five, and Imam Sahl ibn 'Abdullah al-Tustari memorizing some litanies at two, these are among the miracles (karamat) and the matter is not built upon them generally. Yes, if he is found with these qualities, his carrying (tahammul) is absolutely accepted, and for this we did not stipulate a specific age, but it is rare, so understand. And the condition for performance (ada') is perfection of intellect, and it also varies among men, so no specific amount can be fixed, so its cause was made to stand in its place legally, as in travel and hardship. He said: its measure is bulugh (puberty) while being safe from insanity and madness. We only stipulated tamyiz itself for tahammul and its perfection for ada' by analogy on testimony (shahada) because both are reports. And by their acceptance (i.e., the Companions) of 'Abdullah ibn 'Abbas, 'Abdullah ibn al-Zubayr, al-Nu'man ibn Bashir, and Anas ibn Malik, their narrations without questioning them whether they carried before bulugh or after, so it is known that bulugh is not a condition for tahammul. As for stipulating it for ada', its reasoning will come. Know that 'Abdullah ibn 'Abbas was born three years before the Hijra according to al-Waqidi, so his age at the Prophet's death was thirteen years, as in al-Isti'ab. Ibn 'Abd al-Barr said: We narrated from various paths from Sa'id ibn Jubayr from Ibn 'Abbas: 'The Messenger of Allah died and I was ten years old, and I had read al-Muhkam, meaning al-Mufassal.' Then narrated another chain... and al-Bukhari reported that he was nearing puberty at the Farewell Pilgrimage, so his bulugh at the time of tahammul is not verified at all. Likewise 'Abdullah ibn al-Zubayr, the first newborn in Islam after the Hijra by one or two years in the famous opinion... so all his hearings were before bulugh. Likewise al-Nu'man ibn Bashir... and Anas ibn Malik was ten years old when the Prophet arrived and twenty when he died, so most of his hearings were before bulugh, and they accepted it all. And as for what Ibn 'Abd al-Barr reported that he witnessed Badr, his witnessing was not for fighting but for serving the Prophet, for he was his servant, may Allah be pleased with him. So it has become clear to you that the best way in evidence is to say: because their hearings were before bulugh, so understand. And it was argued that the practice of the Salaf was to make children hear, so if their hearings were not accepted, there would be no benefit. But the author (al-Musallam) did not accept this. And he said: 'As for making children hear, it is not necessary (for the desired conclusion) because of the possibility of blessing and familiarity with narration, which are among the greatest benefits.' And it was said: 'The near-adult (murahiq) is accepted in narration and performance, but not absolutely, rather with investigation (taharrin): if it falls on truth, it is accepted; otherwise not.' And it was said in al-Tahrir to refute it: 'The relied upon in this chapter is the Companions, and they did not refer to him (the murahiq).' So he is not accepted. I say: the utmost that follows from this is lack of evidence, but non-existence of evidence does not necessitate non-existence of the indicated. This is not clear, for he deduces from the non-referral on his non-acceptance; non-referral is evidence against it. So it is better to say: perhaps non-referral is due to no need to refer to them, so it does not serve as proof. Rather the face in refuting it is the suspicion of lack of taklif, for the murahiq is not obligated, so lying is not forbidden for him, so it is possible that he lies then. Therefore due to this suspicion he is not accepted, as with the sinful (fasiq), rather more so. Those who accept the murahiq said that the people of Quba' accepted Anas ibn Malik and Ibn 'Umar while they were then not yet baligh. He answered: 'The reliance of the people of Quba' on Anas or Ibn 'Umar was at the age of bulugh, according to the correct view.' But you have known that Anas was ten on the day of the noble arrival, and the change of Qibla was after sixteen or seventeen months, so how could he have been baligh? As for Ibn 'Umar, al-Waqidi said: He was not yet pubescent on the day of Badr, so the Prophet deemed him too young and sent him back, so how could he be baligh at the time of the Qibla change? More amazing than this is what was said: the correct is that the informant was both Anas and Ibn 'Umar, and he was baligh and older than Ibn 'Umar, and they accepted his statement. But it has become clear to you that the matter is opposite. The truth in the answer is that Anas and Ibn 'Umar are narrators, and the informant was other than them. For in the narration of Anas: 'A man from Banu Salama passed by them while they were bowing in Fajr prayer', and in the narration of Ibn 'Umar: 'While the people were in Quba' praying Fajr, a visitor came to them from the other side...' It was said that it was 'Abbad ibn Bishr in al-Taysir. Al-Hafiz al-'Asqalani said: He is more likely. Ibn Khaythama narrated it. In al-Tahrir: It is 'Abbad ibn Nuhayk according to muhaddithun, and he was an old man. 'Abbad ibn Bishr was martyred in Yamama at forty-five. And it appears to this slave that it was the day of the informant for the people of the mosque of Banu Haritha, not for the people of Quba' mosque. And Allah knows best. Then even if it is granted that the informant was Anas or Ibn 'Umar, the utmost that follows is the acceptance of the people of Quba', but it is not a proof. If one clings to the tacit approval of the Prophet, it is denied. Rather they believed in the unseen, so this report did not become a (binding) report, so understand.
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage from Fawatih al-Rahmut comments on the conditions for a narrator in hadith. It first establishes that the condition for tahammul (receiving/learning hadith) is tamyiz (discernment), defined as the ability to understand speech and respond appropriately. This condition is typically not found before age seven, but it can exist earlier as exceptional cases (karamat). For ada' (transmitting/teaching hadith), a higher condition is required: perfection of intellect, which is legally measured by bulugh (puberty) and being free from insanity. The author supports this by analogy (qiyas) to testimony (shahada), since both are forms of reporting. Evidence from Companions like Ibn 'Abbas, Ibn al-Zubayr, Nu'man ibn Bashir, and Anas ibn Malik shows that they transmitted narrations they heard before reaching bulugh, proving that bulugh is not required for tahammul. The passage then addresses the objection that making children listen (isama') does not necessarily imply acceptance of their narrations, as it could be for blessing or familiarity. The discussion then focuses on the murahiq (near-adult): some say he is accepted with investigation, but the preferred view (from al-Tahrir) is that he is not accepted due to the suspicion of lying, since he is not legally obligated (mukallaf). The passage refutes the counterargument from the people of Quba' who accepted Anas and Ibn 'Umar as minor narrators, by showing that the actual informant in that incident was a reliable adult, not the minors themselves. The conclusion is that a minor's narration is not accepted for ada' even if accepted for tahammul.

Key Terms
التحمل (tahammul): Receiving and learning a hadith from a teacher
الأداء (ada'): Transmitting and teaching a hadith to others
التمييز (tamyiz): The ability to understand speech and respond appropriately
البلوغ (bulugh): Reaching puberty, legal majority
المراهق (murahiq): A near-adult, i.e., a child approaching puberty, typically between 13-14 years old

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is required for the performance (ada') of hadith narration?
A) Tamyiz only
B) Bulugh and freedom from insanity
C) Bulugh only
D) Being a Companion

Key Takeaway
For hadith narration, tamyiz is the condition for receiving (tahammul), while bulugh and sanity are required for transmitting (ada'), as established by analogy to testimony and the practice of the Companions.

Condition of Islam for Hadith Narration: Ada' vs Tahammul
Stating that Islam is required for performance but not for receiving hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Islam is required for hadith transmission (ada') but not for receiving (tahammul), and derive this ruling from Quran 49:6 using the Hanafi usul principle regarding the term 'fasiq'.

Core Idea
Islam is required for transmitting hadith, not for hearing it—the narrator's state at narration determines acceptance.

A common question in hadith studies is whether a narrator must be Muslim at the time of hearing a hadith or only when transmitting it. This passage from Fawatih al-Rahmut settles the issue: Islam is a condition for ada' (performance) only, not for tahammul (receiving). The evidence includes a Quranic verse and the consensus on a Companion's case. Let's examine the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State clearly what the passage establishes: Islam is required for the time of narration (ada'), not for the time of hearing (tahammul).
The phrase 'في حال الأداء لا حين التحمل' is key.
2
Examine the evidence for tahammul
The passage cites the case of Jubayr ibn Mut'im, who heard a hadith while a captive (non-Muslim) and later narrated it, accepted by consensus. This shows tahammul does not require Islam.
Also, the reason given: tamyiz (discernment) suffices for hearing.
3
Analyze the dalil for ada'
The Quranic verse (49:6) commands verification of news from a 'fasiq'. The Hanafi interpretation holds that 'fasiq' in the earlier usage includes disbelievers, implying their reports cannot be accepted without verification.
This yields the condition of Islam at the time of narration.
4
Explore the linguistic classification
The term 'fasiq' is general (amm) in the verse, covering both sinful believers and disbelievers. According to Hanafi usul, an 'amm' is qat'i until proven otherwise.
Thus the command to verify applies to reports from any fasiq, including non-Muslims.
5
Note the expansion on innovations
The passage discusses innovations (bida') that entail disbelief, distinguishing between one who commits such innovation (kafir) and one to whom it is attributed but does not believe (not kafir). This nuanced point clarifies the boundary of 'fasiq'.
This is secondary to the main ruling but shows the depth of the discussion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها الإسلام في حال الأداء لا حين التحمل وعدم الاشتراط حين التحمل القبول جبير في قراءة المغرب بـ) سورة الطور) مع أنه تحمل حين جاء أسيراً يوم بدر ( إجماعاً) ولأنه يكفي للتحمل التمييز، وعقل الكافر غير مؤف، وأما الاشتراط أداء فلأنه قال تعالى : إن جَاءَكُم فَاسِقٌ بِنَبَاءِ فَتَيَيّنوا) [الحجرات : ٦] وهو أي الفاسق بالعرف المتقدم يعم الكافر والفاسق) في عرفنا وهو المؤمن المرتكب للكبيرة ( والبدعة المتضمنة (كفراً أي البدعة التي يلزمها الكافر (كالتجسيم كالكفر عند الجماعة (المكفرة) أي عند من يكفر بها كالقاضيين) القاضي أبي بكر الباقلاني، والقاضي عبد الجبار من المعتزلة ( وعند غيره) أي عند غير المكفر، فرقاً بين لزوم الكفر والالتزام فإن الملتزم كافر دون من لزمه وهو لا يرى ذلك ولا يعتقده (كالبدع الجلية، وهي البدعة التي لم تكن عن شبهة قوية معتبرة شرعاً، بحيث لم تكن عذراً شرعاً، لا دنيا ولا آخرة كفسق (الخوارج المبيحة دماء المسلمين وأموالهم وسبي ذراريهم (وفيها) أي
And among them (the conditions) is Islam at the time of performance (ada'), not at the time of carrying (tahammul). And the non-stipulation at the time of tahammul is (supported by the acceptance of) Jubayr (ibn Mut'im) in his recitation of Surah al-Tur in Maghrib, while he had carried (the hadith) when he came as a captive on the day of Badr, by consensus. And because for tahammul, tamyiz suffices, and the intellect of a disbeliever is not trustworthy. As for stipulating it for ada', it is because Allah says: 'If a fasiq comes to you with news, verify...' (49:6). And 'fasiq' in the earlier usage generally includes both the disbeliever and the fasiq in our usage, which is the believer who commits a major sin. And the innovation that entails disbelief (kufr), i.e., the innovation that necessitates disbelief, such as tajsim (anthropomorphism), which is like disbelief according to the group that declares it disbelief, like the two Qadis (Abu Bakr al-Baqillani and 'Abd al-Jabbar from the Mu'tazila). And according to others (who do not declare it disbelief), there is a distinction between the necessity of disbelief and (actual) commitment: the committed (multazim) is a disbeliever, whereas one to whom it is necessary but does not see it nor believe it is not. And like the manifest innovations (bida' jalila), which are innovations not based on a strong legally-considered doubt, such that they are not a legal excuse in this world or the hereafter, like the sin of the Kharijites who permit the blood of Muslims, their wealth, and the taking of their children as captives. And among them (the conditions) is...
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage establishes the condition of Islam for the performance (ada') of hadith narration, but not for tahammul (receiving). The evidence for non-stipulation at tahammul is the case of Jubayr ibn Mut'im, who was a captive (non-Muslim) when he heard a hadith (the Prophet reciting Surah al-Tur in Maghrib), and his narration is accepted by consensus. The reasoning is that tamyiz suffices for tahammul, and the intellect of a disbeliever is not necessarily impaired (though his reliability for transmission is questionable). For ada', the condition of Islam is derived from the Quranic verse (49:6) commanding verification of reports from a 'fasiq'. The term 'fasiq' in earlier usage (of the Salaf) included both disbelievers and sinful believers, though in later usage it is restricted to the latter. The passage then discusses innovations (bida') that entail disbelief, such as tajsim (anthropomorphism), and distinguishes between one who actually commits/embraces such innovation (who becomes a disbeliever) and one to whom it is attributed but does not believe it (not a disbeliever). It also mentions the Kharijites as an example of manifest innovation that does not excuse their sin. The overall ruling: a narrator must be Muslim at the time of transmitting (ada') for his narration to be accepted; his status at the time of hearing (tahammul) is irrelevant.

Key Terms
الفاسق (al-fasiq): In earlier usage: one who deviates from truth, including both disbelievers and sinful believers. In later usage: a believer who commits a major sin.
البدعة المكفرة (al-bid'a al-mukaffira): An innovation that entails disbelief, such as tajsim (anthropomorphism), according to some scholars.
التحمل (al-tahammul): The act of receiving or hearing a hadith from a teacher, with the intention of preserving it for transmission.
الأداء (al-ada'): The act of transmitting or narrating a hadith to others.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary evidence for requiring Islam at the time of hadith narration (ada')?
A) The consensus of the Companions
B) The case of Jubayr ibn Mut'im
C) The Quranic verse about the fasiq
D) The discussion on innovations

Key Takeaway
Islam is a condition for hadith narration only at the time of transmission (ada'), not at the time of receiving (tahammul), based on the Quranic command to verify news from a fasiq, with the term 'fasiq' understood in its broader sense including disbelievers.

The Condition of Dhabt (Accuracy) in Hadith Narration
Definition and justification of dhabt condition in narrator evaluation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define dhabt and explain how it is established, and distinguish it from 'adalah in the context of narrator reliability.

Core Idea
A narrator must be both 'adl and dābit – justice alone does not guarantee accurate transmission.

In Usul al-Fiqh, the reliability of a hadith depends on both the integrity ('adalah) and the precision (dhabt) of its narrator. This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut clarifies the concept of dhabt, how it is determined, and why it is necessary even when 'adalah is present. We will examine the definition, the method of verification, and a common objection resolved by the author.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key condition
Focus on the phrase 'And from them: preferring his accuracy and not being careless in hadith.' The text establishes that dhabt (accuracy) is a required quality, and some scholars add the avoidance of carelessness (tasahul).
Note the nuance: dhabt alone might not prevent error if the narrator is careless.
2
Understand the relationship with 'adalah
The author notes that stipulating 'adalah already precludes carelessness, because a just person is not careless. However, dhabt remains a separate requirement because even a just person can have weak memory or make mistakes in what he believes he remembers.
This is a key distinction: 'adalah ensures truthfulness, but dhabt ensures accuracy.
3
Examine the methods to establish dhabt
The text gives two ways: (1) the narrator's fame (shuhra) for being accurate, and (2) the agreement of his narrations with those of other known accurate narrators. Also, his conduct should mirror that of careful scholars.
These are external indicators; internal scrutiny is also required.
4
Analyze the objection and response
An objector argues that a just person only narrates what he truly remembers, so if he narrates, he must be accurate. The author responds that the just person narrates only what he believes he remembers, but that belief may be mistaken due to forgetfulness or weak memory. Therefore, dhabt is still needed to assure the listener.
The hypothetical objection is answered by distinguishing actual memory from believed memory.
5
Apply the concept to Abu Hurayra's example
The passage mentions that Abu Hurayra was criticized for narrating many hadith, not because he was dishonest, but because quantity increases the risk of error in recall. This illustrates the importance of dhabt even for upright narrators.
This example shows the practical concern behind the condition of dhabt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها رجحان ضبطه وعدم تساهله في الحديث بعضهم اكتفوا بالضبط فقط، والأولى ما ذكره المصنف لأن الضابط ربما يتساهل فيقع في الغلط، إلا أن اشتراط العدالة يغني عن اشتراط عدم التساهل، لأن العدل لا يتساهل فتأمل ليحصل الظن ظن الصدق وطريقه أن يراقب بكليته إلى لفظه ومعنا ويداوم عليه ويتشبث بمذاكرته حتى يؤدي وهذا مبني على أن فهم المعنى شرط الرواية وسيجيء إن شاء الله تعالى ويعرف) الضابط (بالشهرة) أنه ضابط وبموافقة (الضابطين أي يكون حديثه مطابقة لأحاديث الضابطين وتكون سيرته موافقة لسيرة الضابطين بأن يراقب هو ليلاً ونهاراً كما يراقب الضابط (فإن قيل : لا يروى العدل إلا ما ذكر وإلا لم يكن عدلاً، فإذا روى حديثاً وتذكر ارتفع احتمال النسيان والتساهل في الضبط ولذلك أنكر على أبي هريرة الإكثار في الرواية فإن ينافي الضبط ويخل بالعدالة (قلنا) العدل (لا يروي إلا ما يعتقد تذكره لا أنه لا يروي إلا ما يذكر في الواقع لكن السامع لا يطمئن إلا بضبطه لاحتمال السهو والخطأ في اعتقاد التذكر، وهذا لأنه إذا لم يكن ضابطاً وكان قاصر الحفظ احتمل احتمالاً قوياً أنه لعله نسي المتن وتذكر غير ما سمع، وإن كان عدلاً لا يكذب قصداً، فكيف يطمئن السامع بروايته، ولا يحصل الظن بمطابقة الواقع (وليس الإنكار للإكثار (إلا) لأن الإكثار يخاف معه ذلك) أي الخطأ في اعتقاد التذكر (فافهم
And from them: preferring his accuracy and not being careless in hadith. Some sufficed with accuracy only, but what the author mentioned is better, because the accurate person might be careless and thus fall into error. However, stipulating 'adalah makes stipulating non-carelessness unnecessary, because the just person is not careless. So reflect to obtain the presumption of truthfulness. Its method is that he observes fully his wording and meaning, persists in it, and adheres to reviewing it until he narrates. This is based on the understanding that comprehension of meaning is a condition for narration, which will come later, God willing. And the accurate person (al-dabit) is known by fame that he is accurate, and by agreement with other accurate persons, meaning his hadith matches the hadith of accurate persons, and his conduct matches their conduct, such that he observes night and day as the accurate person observes. If it is said: The just person narrates only what he remembers, otherwise he would not be just. So when he narrates a hadith and remembers, the possibility of forgetfulness and carelessness in accuracy is removed. For this reason, Abu Hurayra was criticized for narrating many hadith, as that contradicts accuracy and breaches 'adalah. We say: The just person narrates only what he believes he remembers, not that he narrates only what he actually remembers. But the listener is only at ease with his accuracy due to the possibility of mistake and error in the belief of remembering. This is because if he is not accurate and has weak memory, there is a strong possibility that he forgot the text and remembered other than what he heard. Even if he is just and does not intentionally lie, how can the listener be at ease with his narration? And the presumption of correspondence to reality is not obtained. And the objection to abundance is only because abundance raises fear of that—meaning error in the belief of remembering. So understand.
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage expounds on the condition of dhabt (accuracy and precision) for a narrator of hadith. It begins by noting that some scholars consider dhabt sufficient on its own, but the author prefers the stronger requirement of also avoiding carelessness (tasahul). However, if 'adalah (justice) is already stipulated, it inherently prevents carelessness, so a separate condition is redundant. The method to know if a narrator is dabit is twofold: his fame as such, and the agreement of his narrations with those of other known dabits. A hypothetical objection is raised: a just person only narrates what he genuinely remembers, so his narration should be trustworthy without further check. The response clarifies that the just person narrates only what he believes he remembers, but due to weak memory he may be mistaken in that belief. Hence, the listener requires the narrator to be dabit to achieve a strong presumption of truth. Criticism of Abu Hurayra's many narrations is explained as concern over possible errors in recall, not dishonesty.

Key Terms
ضابط (dābit): A narrator who is precise, accurate, and free from carelessness in memorizing and transmitting hadith.
ضبط (dabt): The quality of being accurate and precise in narration, including full attention to wording and meaning.
تساهل (tasājul): Carelessness or leniency that may lead to error in narration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how is a narrator known to be dābit?
A) By his claim to be accurate.
B) By his fame as accurate and the agreement of his narrations with those of other accurate narrators.
C) By his number of narrations being few.
D) By his age and experience.

Key Takeaway
Dhabt (accuracy) is a distinct condition from 'adalah; a narrator must be both just and precise for his narration to yield the legal presumption of truth (zann) required in Hanafi usul.

The True Condition of 'Adalah: Continuous Practice, Not Inner Quality
Defining 'adalah and clarifying its condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of 'adalah and distinguish between the inner malakah and the actual condition of continuous practice.

Core Idea
'Adalah is proven by observable behavior, not by an invisible inner quality.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut refines the definition of 'adalah (justice) used in evaluating narrators and witnesses. It argues that the condition is not a hidden spiritual quality (malakah) but the continuous external practice of taqwa and muru'ah. Understanding this distinction is crucial for properly assessing reliability in hadith and testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial definition
Note that 'adalah is initially defined as a malakah of taqwa and muru'ah.
2
Analyze the critique
See why the author considers this insufficient: the malakah is hidden and may coexist with committing a sin.
3
Extract the true condition
The condition is the continuous practice (mulāzamat al-taqwā) of avoiding major sins and base actions, and performing obligations.
4
Understand the analogy
The ruling operates on evidence (avoidance), not the inner state, analogous to hardship as evidence for travel concessions.
5
Apply the distinction
Recognize that 'adalah is determined by observable behavior, not presumed inner piety.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها العدالة حال الأداء لا حال التحمل (وهي) أي العدالة (ملكة التقوى والمروءة، والدليل) على هذه الملكة وترك الكبائر من الذنوب والمخل بالمروءة) من الصغائر والأفعال الخسيسة، ولما كانت هذه الملكة خفية أدير الحكم على دليلها كما في السفر والمشقة، وأنت لا يذهب عليك أن المناسب للاشتراط هو الملازمة على التقوى باجتنابه عن المحرمات والأفعال الخسيسة وإتيانه بالواجبات والأفعال المناسبة للمروءة ، وهذا هو الذي يجتنب ويتقي عن الكذب، وأما الملكة فأمر زائد لا دخل فيه، بل الملكة قد يتخلف عنها الاجتناب، فهي لا تنافي إتيان كبيرة مرة فالملازمة على التقوى بترك الكبائر والأفعال الخسيسة هي الشرط، لا أن الشرط حقيقة الملكة، وهذا مظنتها كما في المشقة والسفر فافهم.
And from them: 'adalah at the time of performance, not at the time of hearing. And 'adalah is the quality (malakah) of taqwa and muru'ah. The evidence for this quality is refraining from major sins (kaba'ir) and from things that harm muru'ah among minor sins and base actions. Since this quality is hidden, the ruling is made to operate on its evidence, as in travel and hardship. It should not be lost on you that what is appropriate to stipulate is the actual continuous practice of taqwa by avoiding forbidden things and base actions, and performing obligations and actions suitable to muru'ah. This is the one who avoids and guards against lies. As for the quality, it is an extra matter that has no bearing. Indeed, the quality may be present while avoidance is absent; it does not contradict committing a major sin once. So the continuous practice of taqwa by leaving major sins and base actions is the condition, not that the condition is the actual quality. This is the indicator of it, as in hardship and travel. So understand.
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage discusses the condition of 'adalah (justice) for narrators and witnesses in Hanafi law. It first states that 'adalah is required at the time of narrating (ada'), not merely at the time of hearing (tahammul). It defines 'adalah as a quality (malakah) of taqwa (piety) and muru'ah (chivalry/decency). However, it immediately critiques this definition, arguing that the actual condition is not the inner quality but the external manifestation: constant avoidance of major sins and base actions, and performance of obligations and decent acts. The inner quality is hidden and may coexist with committing a major sin, so it cannot be the real condition. The true condition is the continuous practice of taqwa (mulazamat al-taqwa). The evidence (such as refraining from sins) is the basis for the ruling, not the malakah itself, analogous to hardship as evidence for the ruling of travel concessions. This is a key refinement: it is the actual behavior that establishes 'adalah, not an abstract disposition.

Key Terms
عدالة ('adālah): The quality of being just, consisting in actual continuous practice of taqwa (avoiding major sins and base actions) and muru'ah (performing obligations and decent acts).
ملكة التقوى (malakat al-taqwā): An inner quality of piety that is not the actual condition; it is rather the evidence of 'adalah.
مروءة (murū'ah): Chivalry or decency; avoiding base actions and performing actions that uphold one's dignity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the actual condition for 'adalah?
A) The inner quality (malakah) of taqwa.
B) The continuous practice of taqwa by avoiding major sins and base actions.
C) The absence of any minor sin ever.
D) The absence of innovation.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, 'adalah is established by evidence of continuous avoidance of sins, not by an inner disposition.
