بحقيقته يقتضي أن يكون مال ابنه وجاريته ملكاً له، ولا أقل من أن يحل له الاستمتاع إلا أن الاستيلاد يقتضي الملك فتدخل الجارية في ملكه (وكحربي) معطوف على قوله : كمن زنی دخل دارنا فأسلم فشرب الخمر جاهلاً بالحرمة لا يحد، لأنها ليست بحرام في جميع (الأديان ولم يكن هو عالماً بديننا، فجوّز هو أن يكون في دين الإسلام العياذ بالله فأورث شبهة مسقطة للحدّ (بخلاف الذمي الذي أسلم فشرب الخمر. فإنه يحدّ لأن حرمتها من ضروريات دار الإسلام فمن نشأ فيها يعلم أن الخمر محرمة في الإسلام، فلا يكون هذا الجهل شبهة دارئة للحدّ الثالث : جهل يصلح عذراً وإن لم يكن نشأ عن دليل كمن أسلم في دار الحرب فترك صلوات جاهلاً لزومها في الإسلام، لا قضاء عليه، خلافاً لزفر) رحمه الله ، فهذا الجهل ،عذر لأنه مجبور فيه. وقد ورد في الخبر الصحيح عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : والهجرة تهدم ما قبلها وكل) خطاب نزل ولم يشتهر فجعله عذر) في حقه (أقول : لا ينافي في هذا ما تقدّم من أنه إذا بلغ) الحكم (إلى واحد) من لزم الكل إجماعاً) وعدم التنافي (لأن سماع العذر قد يكون بعد اللزوم) ووجه كونه عذراً أنه لم ينقل عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم أنه ألزم الحكم النازل لجاهل به من وقت النزول أو من وقت الإخبار به للبعض، ولذا لم يأمر أهل قباء بالإعادة، فتأمل (وكالأمة) معطوف على قوله : كمن أسلم المنكوحة إذا جهلت إعتاق المولى فلم تفسخ نكاحها (أو علمت) إعتاقه إياها وجهلت ثبوت الخيار لها شرعاً بالإعتاق لا يبطل خيارها) في الفسخ في الصورتين بخلاف الحرة إذا زوجها غير الأب والجد) من الأولياء (صغيرة فبلغت جاهلة بثبوت حق الفسخ لها، فهذا الجهل لا يكون عذراً ويبطل حق الفسخ (وذلك لأن الدار دار العلم) يمكن التعلم فيها وليس لها ما يشغلها عن التعلم)(۱) البلوغ (بخلاف الأمة) فالجهل بتقصير منها فلا يكون عذراً كذا قالوا وفيه بحث، لأنها كانت قبل البلوغ غير مكلفة بتعلم العلم أصلاً فعدم التعلم قبله يكون عذراً البتة لأنه من غير تقصير فتأمل.
Conclusion on Ijtihad and Taqlid: The prohibition of selling ummahat al-awlad after disagreement among the Companions is established, so it is not definitive. The second type: ignorance that is not an excuse but serves as a shubha (semblance), so it removes what is averted by it, like the killing by one of the two guardians (of the killer) after the other has pardoned — [the killer] is not subject to retaliation even though this killing is transgressive due to the shubha, because it is a place of ijtihad. Some scholars of Medina said that retaliation is not dropped by the pardon of some. If he knew that it was dropped and then killed him intentionally, retaliation is obligatory. Apparently, the issue is assumed in the case where the guardian who killed after the other's pardon believed the permissibility of retaliation. According to this, this ignorance is in a matter of ijtihad, so it is an excuse in this world and the Hereafter absolutely, so this is not an example for this category. And like one who commits zina with his father's slave-girl or his wife, thinking it halal: he is not hadded according to our three imams because of the confusion arising from the familiarity between them in enjoyment of the other's property — so this enjoyment produces a shubha. But it is truly zina, so no lineage is established from this zina even if he claims it, and no iddah because it is specific to what is not zina. Unlike the father's intercourse with his son's slave-girl, because lineage is established if he claims it, she becomes umm walad for him, enters his ownership, and the father must pay her value, because the established shubha here arises from a legal proof, namely his saying (peace be upon him): 'You and your property belong to your father.' In its literal sense, it requires that his son's property and slave-girl are his property, or at least that enjoyment is permissible for him, except that istilad (bearing a child) requires ownership, so the slave-girl enters his ownership. And like a harbi (enemy belligerent) — coordinated with 'like one who commits zina' — who enters our abode and then accepts Islam and drinks wine ignorant of its prohibition: he is not hadded, because it is not prohibited in all religions, and he was not knowledgeable of our religion, so he thought that perhaps in the religion of Islam it is permissible (Allah forbid), so this produced a shubha that drops the hadd. Unlike a dhimmi who accepts Islam and then drinks wine: he is hadded, because its prohibition is among the necessities of Dar al-Islam, and one who grew up there knows that wine is prohibited in Islam, so this ignorance is not a shubha that averts the hadd. The third type: ignorance that is a valid excuse even if it does not arise from a proof, like one who accepts Islam in Dar al-Harb and leaves prayers ignorant of their obligation in Islam: no making up (qada') is required upon him, contrary to Zufar (may Allah have mercy on him). This ignorance is an excuse because he is compelled in it. It is reported in the authentic hadith from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him): 'Hijra erases what came before it.' And every ruling that was revealed and not widely known, He made it an excuse for him. I say: this does not contradict what preceded — that when the ruling reaches one, it becomes binding on all by consensus — and there is no contradiction because the acceptance of the excuse may be after the obligation. The reason it is an excuse is that it is not transmitted from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him and his family and companions) that he imposed a revealed ruling on one ignorant of it from the time of revelation or from the time of informing some, and therefore he did not order the people of Quba' to repeat (their prayer). So ponder. And like the female slave — coordinated with 'like one who accepts Islam' — who is married and is ignorant of her master's manumission, so she does not annul her marriage; or she knows of his manumission but is ignorant that the option (of annulment) is established for her by manumission: her option to annul is not invalidated in both cases. Unlike a free woman who is married off by someone other than the father or grandfather (from guardians) while she is a minor, then she reaches puberty ignorant of the right of annulment for her: this ignorance is not an excuse and her right of annulment is invalidated. That is because the abode is an abode of knowledge where learning is possible and she has nothing to occupy her from learning at the time of puberty, unlike the slave girl: her ignorance is due to her own negligence, so it is not an excuse. Thus they said, but there is discussion in it, because she was not obligated to learn knowledge at all before puberty, so not learning before it is absolutely an excuse because it is without negligence. So ponder.
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Musallam al-Thubut discusses the classification of ignorance (jahl) in legal contexts. The author begins by noting that the prohibition of selling ummahat al-awlad (slave mothers of children) is not definitive because there was disagreement among the Companions. Then he divides ignorance into three types: first, ignorance that is not an excuse but can serve as a shubha (semblance) that averts certain penalties. The example given is a guardian who kills the killer after another guardian has pardoned; because the permissibility of retaliation is a matter of ijtihad, the killer may believe it is still permissible, so he is not subject to qisas despite the killing being transgressive. The second type is ignorance arising from a shubha based on a legal proof, such as a man who commits zina with his father's slave-girl thinking it permissible due to the hadith 'You and your property belong to your father.' This shubha averts the hadd penalty, but the act is still zina in reality, so no lineage or iddah is established. In contrast, if a father has intercourse with his son's slave-girl, it is not zina because of the same hadith, and lineage is established if he claims it. Similarly, a harbi (enemy combatant) who accepts Islam and then drinks wine out of ignorance of its prohibition is not punished, because wine was not prohibited in his former religion. However, a dhimmi who converts and drinks wine is punished, as he grew up knowing it is prohibited in Islam. The third type is ignorance that is a valid excuse even without a shubha, such as a person who accepts Islam in Dar al-Harb and fails to pray out of ignorance; no qada' is required, contrary to Zufar. The author also discusses the case of a slave woman who is ignorant of her manumission or of her option to annul her marriage: her option remains due to the shubha of ignorance, unlike a free woman who reaches puberty in a land of knowledge and fails to learn about her option; her ignorance is not excused. The author then offers a critique: since a minor is not obliged to learn, her ignorance before puberty should be excused. This passage clarifies the nuanced Hanafi position on how ignorance interacts with legal obligations and penalties.

Key Terms
شبهة (shubha): A semblance or doubt that is legally recognized to avert certain penalties, even if the act remains unlawful in reality.
دار الحرب (dar al-harb): A land not under Islamic rule where Islamic laws are not enforced.
جهل (jahl): Lack of knowledge that may or may not be a legal excuse depending on its type.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi classification in this passage, why is a free woman who reaches puberty ignorant of her right to annul her marriage not excused, while a slave woman in the same situation is excused?
A) Because the free woman is wealthier and should hire a lawyer.
B) Because the free woman lives in an abode of knowledge (dar al-ilm) where learning is possible, while the slave woman is occupied with her master's service.
C) Because the slave woman is not required to marry.
D) Because the free woman's marriage contract is invalid.

Key Takeaway
Ignorance is classified into three types in Hanafi usul: as a shubha, as a shubha from a proof, and as a pure excuse; the key determinant is whether the person had access to knowledge and was negligent.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
8 min
The Principle: Ijtihad Rulings Are Not Overturned Unless Contradictory to Qati'
States the principle that ijtihad rulings are not overturned unless contradictory to definitive evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi usul principle that ijtihad rulings are not overturned unless contradictory to a definitive text (qati') and explain the rationale based on preventing endless litigation.

Core Idea
Ijtihad rulings stand unless they contradict a qati' — otherwise, judiciary collapses.

This lesson introduces a foundational rule of usul al-fiqh: rulings issued by a mujtahid judge are not overturned in matters of ijtihad unless they contradict a definitive proof (qati'). The rationale is practical: if every ijtihad could be reversed by a later ijtihad, disputes would never be settled. The text cites consensus (ijma) for this rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule
Read the opening statement: 'لا ينقض الحكم في الاجتهاديات إذا لم يخالف قاطعاً'. State the rule in your own words.
The rule applies only to rulings on ijtihad matters, not to matters where a definitive text exists.
2
Define qati'
List what constitutes a qati' according to the text: Quran, mutawatir and mashhur sunnah, and consensus of the early generation (as per al-Hidayah).
Note that the Hanafi definition of qati' excludes ahad hadith unless it is mashhur.
3
Explain the rationale
Why does the text argue that overturning ijtihad rulings would lead to endless litigation? Because in every dispute a qati' is not available, so if overturning were allowed, it could go on infinitely.
This rationale is based on sadd al-dhara'i' (blocking means to harm).
4
Note the exception
When is a ruling overturned? Only if it contradicts a qati'. In that case, it is overturned immediately.
The text then discusses cases where the ruling is built on something forbidden, leading to overturning even without contradiction to qati' (later lesson).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة): لا ينقض الحكم في الاجتهاديات إذا لم يخالف قاطعاً) وهو الكتاب والسنة المتواترة والمشهور والإجماع وفي «الهداية»: المراد إجماع الأكثر من الصدر الأول (وإلا) يكن كذلك، بل جاز النقض (نقض) هذا النقض أيضاً لاجتهاد لاحق (ويتسلسل الأمر، فتفوت فائدة نصب الحاكم من فصل الخصومات فإنه لا يتيسر في كل خصومة قاطع يقطع ما وراء مجتهد فيه فيتسلسل الأمر ولو) حكم بخلاف اجتهاده كان باطلاً اتفاقاً وإن قلد غيره من المجتهدين يجب عليه العمل بظنه ويحرم اتباع غيره كما مر فإنه ترك لما علمه حكماً إلهياً بما ظنه غير حكم إلهي (ولا يجوز له التقليد مع اجتهاده إجماعاً فينقض ما بنى عليه كذا في شرح المختصر، وأورد عليه أن عدم الحل مسلم ولا يلزم منه عدم النفاذ للحكم ونقضه (كما عرفت قول الإمام أبي حنيفة) وههنا إيرادان : الأول : أن نقل الإجماع ليس في محله فإن الإمام أبا حنيفة قائل بالنفاذ، وهذا الإيراد (لأنه حق. والثاني : أنه لا يصح الاستدلال بعدم الحل على عدم النفاذ فإن الشيء لا يحل ولا ينقض، كالطلاق في الحيض، وهذا ليس بشيء، فإن الحكم كان مبنياً على العمل بخلاف الاجتهاد والمبني على الحرام أورث خبثاً فينقض، ولذا حكم تزوج مجتهد بلا ولي ثم تغير اجتهاده فاختار ابن الحاجب التحريم اتصل به حکم حاكم أم لا لأنه مستديم لما يعتقده حراماً، أقول فيه : أن) صحة (البقاء فرع صحة الانعقاد وقد كان يعتقد صحته وقت الانعقاد فهو منعقد فكان كنقض الحكم تدبر) وفيه أنه وإن كان يعتقد قبل أنه صحيح، لكن الآن اعتقد أن ما كنت زعمت جهل مرکب والنكاح كان فاسداً فيلزم الاستدامة على ما اعتقد أنه حرام من الأصل، وهذا بخلاف نكاح الكافر من غير شهود عند أبي حنيفة، فإنهم لما لم يكونوا مأمورين وكان ذلك جائزاً عندهم فقد انعقد النكاح في نفسه الأمر فلا يفسخ بالإيمان لأنه عاصم، وأما ههنا فقد اعتقد أنه كان مكلفاً بالتعبد بالفساد واعتقاد الصحة جهلاً مركباً، فتأمل ففيه نظر (وقيل) التحريم (إن لم يتصل به حكم حاكم وإلا فالإباحة قال المصنف (وهو الأشبه بالصواب (لأن القضاء يرفع حكم الخلاف كما مر في إبطال التصويب) وهذا غير وافٍ فإن القضاء يرفع الخلاف، فإن لاقي محلاً مختلفاً فيه نفذ ولا ينقض، لا أنه يجعل ما كان في معتقده حراماً حلالاً، نعم : قد ذهب الإمام إلى أن القضاء لوجود الأسباب بشهود الزور ينفذ ظاهراً وباطناً، وأين هذا من ذلك (ولا خلاف فيه لأحد إلا ما عن أبي يوسف في مجتهد طلق البتة، فقضى بالرجعة ومعتقده البينونة يأخذ بها أي بالبينونة، ولا يلتفت إلى القضاء (فتأمل) ووجهه أيضاً ما ذكرنا أن معتقد المطلق أن الحكم الإلهي التحريم، فلو أخذ بالقضاء لزم ارتكاب ما هو محرم في معتقده إلا أن يجعل القضاء حلالاً في المجتهد فيه فافهم ولو كان المتزوج مقلداً ثم علم تغير اجتهاد إمامه فكذلك) الاختلاف، فعند البعض يأخذ بالتحريم، وعند البعض كذلك إلا أن يتعلق به القضاء، وهذا موقوف على أن المقلد لا يجوز له ترك تقليد إمامه (وقيل : لا يجب على المقلد المفارقة مطلقاً لأنه ليس للمقلد معتقد إنما كان العلم على حسب فتوى إمامه، فإذا رجع الإمام فله أن يبقى على القول المرجوع عنه، لأن المرجوع عنه والمرجوع إليه سواء اللهم إلا إن صار برجوعه مجمعاً عليه فحينئذ اختار المرجوع إليه .
Issue: A ruling is not overturned in ijtihad matters if it does not contradict a definitive text, which is the Book, the Mutawatir and Mashhur Sunnah, and Consensus. And in al-Hidayah: what is meant is the consensus of the majority of the early generation. Otherwise, if it is not so, rather is it permissible to overturn, then this overturning is also overturned by a later ijtihad, and the matter becomes endless. Thus the benefit of appointing a judge for settling disputes is lost, because in every dispute a definitive text that cuts off what is beyond a matter of ijtihad is not available, so it becomes endless. Even if he judges contrary to his ijtihad, it is void by agreement. And if he follows another mujtahid, he must act on his own opinion and it is prohibited to follow others, as has passed, because he has left what he knew as a divine ruling for what he thought was not a divine ruling. And he is not permitted to follow with his ijtihad by consensus, so what was built upon it is overturned. This is in Sharh al-Mukhtasar. And it was objected that its not being permissible is granted, but it does not necessitate its non-enforceability and overturning, as you know the statement of Imam Abu Hanifa. Here are two objections: First: reporting consensus is out of place, for Imam Abu Hanifa says it is enforceable, and this objection is correct. Second: it is not valid to infer from the lack of permissibility the lack of enforceability, because a thing may be impermissible yet not overturned, like divorce during menstruation. And this is nothing, for the judgment was based on acting contrary to ijtihad, and what is built on the forbidden causes impurity so it is overturned. Hence the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) ruled for overturning, and this is very clear in the case of intent, and in forgetfulness also there is no clinging. Also in this judgment there is giving the property of one to another by force, and he has no right to it, so it is like usurpation, so the judgment is overturned and the property is returned. So understand. Absolutely. (Branch: If a mujtahid marries without a guardian then his ijtihad changes, Ibn al-Hajib chose prohibition, connected to the judge's ruling or not, because he is perpetuating what he believes is forbidden. I say: The validity of continuation depends on the validity of the contract, and at the time of the contract he believed it valid, so it is contracted, so it is like overturning a ruling, ponder. And in it: Although he previously believed it correct, now he believes that what I thought was compound ignorance and the marriage was invalid, so he is required to continue on what he believes was forbidden from the beginning. This differs from the marriage of a disbeliever without witnesses according to Abu Hanifa, for they were not commanded and it was permissible for them, so the marriage itself was contracted, so it is not annulled upon embracing Islam because it is preserved. But here he believed he was obligated by worship to consider it invalid and believing it valid was compound ignorance, so reflect, for there is consideration. And it is said: Prohibition if the judge's ruling is not connected, otherwise permissibility. The author said: This is more like correctness, because the judge's ruling removes the disagreement as mentioned in nullifying taswib. And this is insufficient, for the judge's ruling removes the disagreement, so if it meets a matter of disagreement it is enforced and not overturned, not that it makes what was in his belief forbidden into permissible. Yes, Imam (Abu Hanifa) held that the judge's ruling due to false witnesses is enforced in form and reality. And where is this compared to that? And there is no disagreement among anyone except what is reported from Abu Yusuf about a mujtahid who divorced irrevocably, and the judge ruled for return, and his belief was final separation: he takes by it, i.e. by final separation, and does not heed the judge's ruling. Ponder. Its reason is also what we mentioned: the divorcer believes the divine ruling to be prohibition, so if he takes by the judge's ruling he would commit what is forbidden in his belief, unless the judge's ruling makes it permissible in matters of ijtihad. So understand. And if the married person was a follower then he learns of the change in his imam's ijtihad, likewise the disagreement. So according to some he takes the prohibition, and according to some likewise unless it is connected to a judge's ruling. This is conditional on the follower being not permitted to leave his imam's taqlid. And it is said: The follower is not required to separate absolutely, because the follower has no conviction; knowledge is only based on his imam's fatwa. So if the imam retracts, he may remain on the retracted opinion, because the retracted and the retained are equal, unless by the imam's retraction it becomes a matter of consensus, then he chooses the retained.

Commentary
This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut discusses a key usul rule: rulings made by a mujtahid are not overturned in ijtihad matters unless they contradict a definitive text (Quran, mutawatir/mashhur sunnah, or consensus). The author explains why: if every ijtihad ruling could be overturned by a later ijtihad, judiciary would collapse. The passage then addresses objections and exceptions. It mentions Imam Abu Hanifa's view that rulings contrary to ijtihad are enforceable, but the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold they are null. A branch case is examined: a mujtahid marries without a guardian, then changes his ijtihad to prohibition. The discussion involves whether the marriage remains valid or is overturned. The author presents multiple opinions, including the importance of whether a judge has ruled. The passage ends with a note on followers (muqallids): if a follower's imam retracts a ruling, the follower may remain on the old ruling unless it contradicts consensus.

Key Terms
الاجتهاديات (al-ijtihādiyyāt): Matters that are subject to ijtihad, i.e., not explicitly ruled by a definitive text.
القاطع (al-qāṭiʿ): A definitive proof from Quran, mutawatir sunnah, mashhur sunnah, or consensus.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, when is a ruling in ijtihad matters overturned?
A) Whenever a later mujtahid disagrees
B) Only if it contradicts a definitive text (qati')
C) Only if the ruler changes his opinion
D) Only if it violates public interest

Key Takeaway
Ijtihad rulings are stable unless they conflict with a qati' text, ensuring finality in judicial decisions.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Overturning and Branch Cases
Discusses the intra-Hanafi dispute on overturning rulings and applies the principle to specific branches.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the enforceability of rulings based on ijtihad, and apply the rule to branch cases involving change of ijtihad in marriage and divorce.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa: rulings contrary to ijtihad are enforceable; Sahibayn: they are overturned because built on impermissible acts.

Having established the general rule, the passage now delves into a key intra-Hanafi disagreement. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that a judge's ruling that contradicts his own ijtihad is still enforceable (nafidh), while his two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, argue it must be overturned (naqd). The text then examines branch cases: a mujtahid who marries without a guardian and later changes his ijtihad, and a case of divorce with a subsequent contradictory ruling. These examples test the limits of the principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
State Abu Hanifa's view (ruling is enforceable not overturned) and the Sahibayn's view (ruling must be overturned because built on something forbidden).
The text uses the terms 'نفاذ' vs 'نقض'.
2
Analyze the evidence for each position
Abu Hanifa's dalil: preservation of judicial finality; Sahibayn's dalil: a ruling built on a forbidden foundation is impure and must be reversed.
The text gives an example: judgment giving property without right is like usurpation.
3
Apply to the marriage branch
A mujtahid marries without a guardian (valid in his ijtihad). Later his ijtihad changes to requiring a guardian. Is the marriage still valid? The text discusses whether the persistence of the marriage (baqa') depends on the original contract or the current belief.
Arguments hinge on whether continuation of marriage is a new contract or continuation of the old.
4
Apply to the divorce branch
A mujtahid divorces irrevocably (battah), but a judge rules for return (raj'ah). According to Abu Yusuf, the divorcer follows his own belief (final separation) and ignores the judge's ruling.
This shows the tension between a judge's ruling and individual ijtihad.
5
Consider the follower (muqallid) case
If a follower's imam changes his ijtihad, the follower may remain on the old ruling unless the new ruling becomes consensus.
This is because the follower has no personal ijtihad; his knowledge is based on the imam's fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة): لا ينقض الحكم في الاجتهاديات إذا لم يخالف قاطعاً) وهو الكتاب والسنة المتواترة والمشهور والإجماع وفي «الهداية»: المراد إجماع الأكثر من الصدر الأول (وإلا) يكن كذلك، بل جاز النقض (نقض) هذا النقض فكان كنقض الحكم تدبر) وفيه أنه وإن كان يعتقد قبل أنه صحيح، لكن الآن اعتقد أن ما كنت زعمت جهل مرکب والنكاح كان فاسداً فيلزم الاستدامة على ما اعتقد أنه حرام من الأصل، وهذا بخلاف نكاح الكافر من غير شهود عند أبي حنيفة، فإنهم لما لم يكونوا مأمورين وكان ذلك جائزاً عندهم فقد انعقد النكاح في نفسه الأمر فلا يفسخ بالإيمان لأنه عاصم، وأما ههنا فقد اعتقد أنه كان مكلفاً بالتعبد بالفساد واعتقاد الصحة جهلاً مركباً، فتأمل ففيه نظر (وقيل) التحريم (إن لم يتصل به حكم حاكم وإلا فالإباحة قال المصنف (وهو الأشبه بالصواب (لأن القضاء يرفع حكم الخلاف كما مر في إبطال التصويب) وهذا غير وافٍ فإن القضاء يرفع الخلاف، فإن لاقي محلاً مختلفاً فيه نفذ ولا ينقض، لا أنه يجعل ما كان في معتقده حراماً حلالاً، نعم : قد ذهب الإمام إلى أن القضاء لوجود الأسباب بشهود الزور ينفذ ظاهراً وباطناً، وأين هذا من ذلك (ولا خلاف فيه لأحد إلا ما عن أبي يوسف في مجتهد طلق البتة، فقضى بالرجعة ومعتقده البينونة يأخذ بها أي بالبينونة، ولا يلتفت إلى القضاء (فتأمل) ووجهه أيضاً ما ذكرنا أن معتقد المطلق أن الحكم الإلهي التحريم، فلو أخذ بالقضاء لزم ارتكاب ما هو محرم في معتقده إلا أن يجعل القضاء حلالاً في المجتهد فيه فافهم ولو كان المتزوج مقلداً ثم علم تغير اجتهاد إمامه فكذلك) الاختلاف، فعند البعض يأخذ بالتحريم، وعند البعض كذلك إلا أن يتعلق به القضاء، وهذا موقوف على أن المقلد لا يجوز له ترك تقليد إمامه (وقيل : لا يجب على المقلد المفارقة مطلقاً لأنه ليس للمقلد معتقد إنما كان العلم على حسب فتوى إمامه، فإذا رجع الإمام فله أن يبقى على القول المرجوع عنه، لأن المرجوع عنه والمرجوع إليه سواء اللهم إلا إن صار برجوعه مجمعاً عليه فحينئذ اختار المرجوع إليه .
Issue: A ruling is not overturned in ijtihad matters if it does not contradict a definitive text, which is the Book, the Mutawatir and Mashhur Sunnah, and Consensus. And in al-Hidayah: what is meant is the consensus of the majority of the early generation. Otherwise, if it is not so, rather is it permissible to overturn, then this overturning is also overturned by a later ijtihad, and the matter becomes endless. Thus the benefit of appointing a judge for settling disputes is lost, because in every dispute a definitive text that cuts off what is beyond a matter of ijtihad is not available, so it becomes endless. Even if he judges contrary to his ijtihad, it is void by agreement. And if he follows another mujtahid, he must act on his own opinion and it is prohibited to follow others, as has passed, because he has left what he knew as a divine ruling for what he thought was not a divine ruling. And he is not permitted to follow with his ijtihad by consensus, so what was built upon it is overturned. This is in Sharh al-Mukhtasar. And it was objected that its not being permissible is granted, but it does not necessitate its non-enforceability and overturning, as you know the statement of Imam Abu Hanifa. Here are two objections: First: reporting consensus is out of place, for Imam Abu Hanifa says it is enforceable, and this objection is correct. Second: it is not valid to infer from the lack of permissibility the lack of enforceability, because a thing may be impermissible yet not overturned, like divorce during menstruation. And this is nothing, for the judgment was based on acting contrary to ijtihad, and what is built on the forbidden causes impurity so it is overturned. Hence the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) ruled for overturning, and this is very clear in the case of intent, and in forgetfulness also there is no clinging. Also in this judgment there is giving the property of one to another by force, and he has no right to it, so it is like usurpation, so the judgment is overturned and the property is returned. So understand. Absolutely. (Branch: If a mujtahid marries without a guardian then his ijtihad changes, Ibn al-Hajib chose prohibition, connected to the judge's ruling or not, because he is perpetuating what he believes is forbidden. I say: The validity of continuation depends on the validity of the contract, and at the time of the contract he believed it valid, so it is contracted, so it is like overturning a ruling, ponder. And in it: Although he previously believed it correct, now he believes that what I thought was compound ignorance and the marriage was invalid, so he is required to continue on what he believes was forbidden from the beginning. This differs from the marriage of a disbeliever without witnesses according to Abu Hanifa, for they were not commanded and it was permissible for them, so the marriage itself was contracted, so it is not annulled upon embracing Islam because it is preserved. But here he believed he was obligated by worship to consider it invalid and believing it valid was compound ignorance, so reflect, for there is consideration. And it is said: Prohibition if the judge's ruling is not connected, otherwise permissibility. The author said: This is more like correctness, because the judge's ruling removes the disagreement as mentioned in nullifying taswib. And this is insufficient, for the judge's ruling removes the disagreement, so if it meets a matter of disagreement it is enforced and not overturned, not that it makes what was in his belief forbidden into permissible. Yes, Imam (Abu Hanifa) held that the judge's ruling due to false witnesses is enforced in form and reality. And where is this compared to that? And there is no disagreement among anyone except what is reported from Abu Yusuf about a mujtahid who divorced irrevocably, and the judge ruled for return, and his belief was final separation: he takes by it, i.e. by final separation, and does not heed the judge's ruling. Ponder. Its reason is also what we mentioned: the divorcer believes the divine ruling to be prohibition, so if he takes by the judge's ruling he would commit what is forbidden in his belief, unless the judge's ruling makes it permissible in matters of ijtihad. So understand. And if the married person was a follower then he learns of the change in his imam's ijtihad, likewise the disagreement. So according to some he takes the prohibition, and according to some likewise unless it is connected to a judge's ruling. This is conditional on the follower being not permitted to leave his imam's taqlid. And it is said: The follower is not required to separate absolutely, because the follower has no conviction; knowledge is only based on his imam's fatwa. So if the imam retracts, he may remain on the retracted opinion, because the retracted and the retained are equal, unless by the imam's retraction it becomes a matter of consensus, then he chooses the retained.
Source pages p. 428

Commentary
This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut discusses a key usul rule: rulings made by a mujtahid are not overturned in ijtihad matters unless they contradict a definitive text (Quran, mutawatir/mashhur sunnah, or consensus). The author explains why: if every ijtihad ruling could be overturned by a later ijtihad, judiciary would collapse. The passage then addresses objections and exceptions. It mentions Imam Abu Hanifa's view that rulings contrary to ijtihad are enforceable, but the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold they are null. A branch case is examined: a mujtahid marries without a guardian, then changes his ijtihad to prohibition. The discussion involves whether the marriage remains valid or is overturned. The author presents multiple opinions, including the importance of whether a judge has ruled. The passage ends with a note on followers (muqallids): if a follower's imam retracts a ruling, the follower may remain on the old ruling unless it contradicts consensus.

Key Terms
النقض (al-naqd): Overturning or nullifying a judicial ruling.
النفاذ (al-nafādh): Enforceability: a ruling that is carried out and not overturned.
المقلد (al-muqallid): A follower who does not perform ijtihad but follows a mujtahid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the intra-Hanafi dispute, what is the basis for the Sahibayn's position that a ruling must be overturned?
A) The ruling contradicts a qati' text
B) The ruling is built on a forbidden act (acting contrary to ijtihad)
C) The ruling was made by a non-mujtahid
D) The ruling was not ratified by a higher authority

Key Takeaway
Within the Hanafi school, Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn diverge on whether a ruling made contrary to the judge's ijtihad should be overturned, with the Sahibayn emphasizing the taint of the forbidden act.

The Definition of Taqlid in Hanafi Usul
Defines taqlid and its boundaries

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define taqlid precisely according to Hanafi usul and distinguish it from following a proof.

Core Idea
Taqlid is acting on another's statement without a proof — following the Prophet or Ijma is not taqlid.

In this lesson, we unpack the precise definition of taqlid as given in Fawatih al-Rahmut. Taqlid is often misunderstood as any form of following; here we see its technical meaning in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition
Locate the precise Arabic wording of the definition: 'العمل بقول الغير من غير حجة متعلق بالعمل'
Memorize this phrasing as it is the standard Hanafi definition.
2
Break down the components
Analyze each part: 'عمل' (action), 'بقول الغير' (upon another's statement), 'من غير حجة' (without evidence), 'متعلق بالعمل' (related to the action).
The 'hujja' here means one of the four primary sources (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas).
3
Understand the exceptions
Note that following the Prophet directly or ijma is not taqlid because those are themselves proofs.
The text says: 'فالرجوع إلى النبي... ليس منه فإنه رجوع إلى الدليل'
4
Distinguish return from action
The mere return to a mufti is not taqlid, but subsequent action based on that return is taqlid if done without independent evidence.
This nuance is crucial for understanding the boundaries of taqlid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل التقليد: العمل بقول الغير من غير حجة متعلق بالعمل والمراد بالحجة حجة من الحجج الأربع، وإلا فقول المجتهد دليله وحجته (كأخذ العامي) من المجتهد (و) أخذ المجتهد من مثله فالرجوع إلى النبي عليه وآله وأصحابه الصلاة والسلام أو إلى الإجماع ليس منه فإنه رجوع إلى الدليل (وكذا ) رجوع العامي إلى المفتي والقاضي إلى العدول) ليس هذا الرجوع نفسه تقليداً وإن كان العمل بما أخذوا بعده تقليداً لإيجاب النص ذلك عليهما) فهو عمل بحجة لا بقول الغير فقط (لكن العرف دل على أن العامي مقلد للمجتهد بالرجوع إليه (قال الإمام) إمام الحرمين (وعليه معظم (الأصوليين وهو المشتهر المعتمد عليه (والمفتي المجتهد من حيث يجيب السائل فهو أخص منه (والمستفتي يقابله) أي السائل من المجتهد من حيث هو سائل (وقد يجتمعان في شخص واحد بناء على التجزي) في الاجتهاد، فيكون في بعض المسائل مجتهداً مفتياً. وفي بعضها مستفتياً لتعدد الجهات والمستفتى فيه الذي وقع السؤال عنه المسائل الشرعية والعقلية على المذهب الصحيح لصحة إيمان المقلد عند الأئمة الأربعة الإمام أبي حنيفة والإمام الشافعي والإمام مالك والإمام أحمد بن حنبل رضوان الله تعالى عليهم وكثير من المتكلمين خلافاً للأشعري. وإن كان آثماً في ترك النظر والاستدلال، أما قبول إيمان المقلد فثابت بالدلائل القطعية فإنه تواتر أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كان يقبل إيمان كل أحد وإن حصل من دول نظر، حتى من الصبيان الذين لم يقدروا على النظر أصلاً، وكذا تواتر من الصحابة والتابعين من غير نكير والخلاف إنما نشأ بعدهم، وأما التأثيم بترك النظر فلم ينص عليه الأئمة، إنما حكم المتأخرون به من جهة ترك النظر الذي كان واجباً. وهذا ليس بشيء، فإن النظر ما كان واجباً إلا لتحصيل الإيمان، وإذا حصل الإيمان ارتفع سبب وجوبه، فلا إثم في الترك كما إذا أسلم الكفار قاطبة سقط الجهاد الذي كان وجب من غير إثم فافهم .
Taqlid: acting upon the statement of another without evidence related to the action. What is meant by evidence is one of the four proofs. Otherwise, the statement of a mujtahid is his proof and evidence. Like the layperson taking from the mujtahid, and the mujtahid taking from his like. Thus, returning to the Prophet (peace be upon him and his family) or to consensus is not included in this, for it is a return to evidence. Likewise, the layperson’s return to the mufti and the judge’s return to the upright witnesses: this return itself is not taqlid, although acting upon what they have taken afterwards is taqlid, because the text obliges that upon them. So it is acting upon evidence, not merely upon another's statement. But custom indicates that the layperson is a muqallid of the mujtahid by returning to him. Al-Imam (Imam al-Haramayn) said: 'And upon it are most of the usuliyyun, and it is the well-known and relied-upon view. The mufti mujtahid, inasmuch as he answers the questioner, is more specific than him, and the mustafti is his counterpart, i.e., the questioner from the mujtahid inasmuch as he is a questioner. They may be combined in one person based on partial ijtihad, so he may be a mujtahid mufti in some issues and a mustafti in others due to multiple aspects. The matters about which inquiry is made are legal and rational issues according to the correct doctrine of the soundness of the faith of the muqallid according to the four imams... and many theologians, contrary to al-Ash'ari. Although he is sinful for abandoning reflection and inference, as for accepting the faith of the muqallid, it is established by definitive proofs, for it is mutawatir that the Messenger of Allah (saw) used to accept the faith of everyone, even if it occurred without reflection, even from children who could not reflect at all. Similarly, it is mutawatir from the Companions and the Followers without objection, and the disagreement arose only after them. As for declaring sinful for abandoning reflection, the imams did not state this; only later scholars ruled from the perspective of abandoning reflection which was obligatory. But this is nothing, for reflection was only obligatory to attain faith, and when faith is attained, the cause of its obligation is removed, so there is no sin in abandoning it, just as if all disbelievers embrace Islam, jihad which was obligatory falls without sin. So understand.
Source pages p. 432

Commentary
This passage from 'Fawatih al-Rahmut' defines the term taqlid in the Hanafi usul tradition. The author begins by giving a precise definition: acting upon the statement of another without a proof (hujja) that is specifically related to the action. He clarifies that the hujja here means one of the four primary sources (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas). The statement of a mujtahid himself is his dalil, so when a layperson follows a mujtahid, he is not following a proof but rather the mujtahid's opinion that is based on proof. Hence, this is taqlid. However, referring directly to the Prophet (saw) or to Ijma is not taqlid because those are themselves proofs. The author further distinguishes between the act of returning to an authority and the act of acting upon that authority's statement. The return itself is not taqlid, but the subsequent action is taqlid if done without independent evidence. Custom assigns the layperson as a muqallid. The passage then discusses the possibility of a person being both a mujtahid and a muqallid in different matters, based on the concept of partial ijtihad. Finally, it addresses a related issue: the validity of the faith of a muqallid. The four imams and many theologians affirm its validity, contrary to al-Ash'ari, although the muqallid may be sinful for not undertaking nazar (reflection). The author argues that nazar was only obligatory to attain faith; once faith is obtained, the obligation ceases. The example of jihad falling if all disbelievers accept Islam is given as an analogy.

Key Terms
التقليد (al-taqlid): العمل بقول الغير من غير حجة متعلق بالعمل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the definition of taqlid?
A) Acting upon a proof
B) Acting upon another's statement without evidence
C) Following the Prophet directly
D) Blind imitation without any basis

Key Takeaway
Taqlid is acting on another's statement without a proof; following the Prophet or Ijma is not taqlid because they are proofs.

Roles in Taqlid: The Muqallid, the Mujtahid, and Partial Ijtihad
Explains the scope of taqlid and the roles of mufti and mustafti

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the relationship between the muqallid and the mujtahid, and identify the concept of partial ijtihad.

Core Idea
A person can be both a mujtahid and a muqallid in different issues due to partial ijtihad.

Building on the definition of taqlid, this lesson explores who is a muqallid and who is a mujtahid. The text clarifies that custom designates the layperson as a muqallid, and that a mujtahid can also be a muqallid in areas outside his expertise.

Guided Path
1
Identify the role of the layperson
The text states: 'لكن العرف دل على أن العامي مقلد للمجتهد بالرجوع إليه' — custom shows that the layperson is a muqallid of the mujtahid by virtue of returning to him.
This is a practical designation based on common practice.
2
Understand the roles of mufti and mustafti
The mufti (mujtahid) answers questions; the mustafti (questioner) seeks answers. These roles are relative: a mujtahid can be a mustafti in another matter.
The text says: 'والمفتي المجتهد من حيث يجيب السائل فهو أخص منه والمستفتي يقابله'
3
Grasp the concept of partial ijtihad
Ijtihad can be partial (tajazzi). A person may be a mujtahid in some issues and a muqallid in others, depending on his expertise.
This is a key Hanafi principle that allows for specialization.
4
Apply the concept
Given partial ijtihad, one person can simultaneously be a mufti for one issue and a mustafti for another.
Example: A scholar expert in inheritance law asks another scholar about a medical fiqh issue.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل التقليد: العمل بقول الغير من غير حجة متعلق بالعمل والمراد بالحجة حجة من الحجج الأربع، وإلا فقول المجتهد دليله وحجته (كأخذ العامي) من المجتهد (و) أخذ المجتهد من مثله فالرجوع إلى النبي عليه وآله وأصحابه الصلاة والسلام أو إلى الإجماع ليس منه فإنه رجوع إلى الدليل (وكذا ) رجوع العامي إلى المفتي والقاضي إلى العدول) ليس هذا الرجوع نفسه تقليداً وإن كان العمل بما أخذوا بعده تقليداً لإيجاب النص ذلك عليهما) فهو عمل بحجة لا بقول الغير فقط (لكن العرف دل على أن العامي مقلد للمجتهد بالرجوع إليه (قال الإمام) إمام الحرمين (وعليه معظم (الأصوليين وهو المشتهر المعتمد عليه (والمفتي المجتهد من حيث يجيب السائل فهو أخص منه (والمستفتي يقابله) أي السائل من المجتهد من حيث هو سائل (وقد يجتمعان في شخص واحد بناء على التجزي) في الاجتهاد، فيكون في بعض المسائل مجتهداً مفتياً. وفي بعضها مستفتياً لتعدد الجهات والمستفتى فيه الذي وقع السؤال عنه المسائل الشرعية والعقلية على المذهب الصحيح لصحة إيمان المقلد عند الأئمة الأربعة الإمام أبي حنيفة والإمام الشافعي والإمام مالك والإمام أحمد بن حنبل رضوان الله تعالى عليهم وكثير من المتكلمين خلافاً للأشعري. وإن كان آثماً في ترك النظر والاستدلال، أما قبول إيمان المقلد فثابت بالدلائل القطعية فإنه تواتر أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كان يقبل إيمان كل أحد وإن حصل من دول نظر، حتى من الصبيان الذين لم يقدروا على النظر أصلاً، وكذا تواتر من الصحابة والتابعين من غير نكير والخلاف إنما نشأ بعدهم، وأما التأثيم بترك النظر فلم ينص عليه الأئمة، إنما حكم المتأخرون به من جهة ترك النظر الذي كان واجباً. وهذا ليس بشيء، فإن النظر ما كان واجباً إلا لتحصيل الإيمان، وإذا حصل الإيمان ارتفع سبب وجوبه، فلا إثم في الترك كما إذا أسلم الكفار قاطبة سقط الجهاد الذي كان وجب من غير إثم فافهم .
Taqlid: acting upon the statement of another without evidence related to the action. What is meant by evidence is one of the four proofs. Otherwise, the statement of a mujtahid is his proof and evidence. Like the layperson taking from the mujtahid, and the mujtahid taking from his like. Thus, returning to the Prophet (peace be upon him and his family) or to consensus is not included in this, for it is a return to evidence. Likewise, the layperson’s return to the mufti and the judge’s return to the upright witnesses: this return itself is not taqlid, although acting upon what they have taken afterwards is taqlid, because the text obliges that upon them. So it is acting upon evidence, not merely upon another's statement. But custom indicates that the layperson is a muqallid of the mujtahid by returning to him. Al-Imam (Imam al-Haramayn) said: 'And upon it are most of the usuliyyun, and it is the well-known and relied-upon view. The mufti mujtahid, inasmuch as he answers the questioner, is more specific than him, and the mustafti is his counterpart, i.e., the questioner from the mujtahid inasmuch as he is a questioner. They may be combined in one person based on partial ijtihad, so he may be a mujtahid mufti in some issues and a mustafti in others due to multiple aspects. The matters about which inquiry is made are legal and rational issues according to the correct doctrine of the soundness of the faith of the muqallid according to the four imams... and many theologians, contrary to al-Ash'ari. Although he is sinful for abandoning reflection and inference, as for accepting the faith of the muqallid, it is established by definitive proofs, for it is mutawatir that the Messenger of Allah (saw) used to accept the faith of everyone, even if it occurred without reflection, even from children who could not reflect at all. Similarly, it is mutawatir from the Companions and the Followers without objection, and the disagreement arose only after them. As for declaring sinful for abandoning reflection, the imams did not state this; only later scholars ruled from the perspective of abandoning reflection which was obligatory. But this is nothing, for reflection was only obligatory to attain faith, and when faith is attained, the cause of its obligation is removed, so there is no sin in abandoning it, just as if all disbelievers embrace Islam, jihad which was obligatory falls without sin. So understand.
Source pages p. 432

Commentary
This passage from 'Fawatih al-Rahmut' defines the term taqlid in the Hanafi usul tradition. The author begins by giving a precise definition: acting upon the statement of another without a proof (hujja) that is specifically related to the action. He clarifies that the hujja here means one of the four primary sources (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas). The statement of a mujtahid himself is his dalil, so when a layperson follows a mujtahid, he is not following a proof but rather the mujtahid's opinion that is based on proof. Hence, this is taqlid. However, referring directly to the Prophet (saw) or to Ijma is not taqlid because those are themselves proofs. The author further distinguishes between the act of returning to an authority and the act of acting upon that authority's statement. The return itself is not taqlid, but the subsequent action is taqlid if done without independent evidence. Custom assigns the layperson as a muqallid. The passage then discusses the possibility of a person being both a mujtahid and a muqallid in different matters, based on the concept of partial ijtihad. Finally, it addresses a related issue: the validity of the faith of a muqallid. The four imams and many theologians affirm its validity, contrary to al-Ash'ari, although the muqallid may be sinful for not undertaking nazar (reflection). The author argues that nazar was only obligatory to attain faith; once faith is obtained, the obligation ceases. The example of jihad falling if all disbelievers accept Islam is given as an analogy.

Key Terms
مستفتي (mustafti): السائل من المجتهد من حيث هو سائل
التجزي في الاجتهاد (al-tajazzi fi al-ijtihad): كون الشخص مجتهداً في بعض المسائل دون بعض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the relied-upon view regarding the layperson's status?
A) The layperson is not a muqallid because he returns to the mufti
B) The layperson is a muqallid by custom
C) The layperson is a mujtahid
D) The layperson is independent of the mujtahid

Key Takeaway
Custom and partial ijtihad allow a person to be both a mujtahid and a muqallid in different matters.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
advanced
10 min
The Validity of a Muqallid's Faith
Defends the validity of the muqallid's faith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the validity of a muqallid's faith and evaluate the argument that abandoning nazar does not invalidate faith.

Core Idea
The faith of a muqallid is valid even if he abandons reflection; the obligation of reflection drops once faith is attained.

This lesson addresses a theological-legal issue: Can a person who merely imitates others in belief be considered a true believer? The Hanafi school affirms it, based on the Prophet's practice and the fall of obligation once the goal is achieved.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
The passage mentions that the four imams and many theologians hold that the faith of a muqallid is sound, contrary to al-Ash'ari.
Al-Ash'ari reportedly rejected the faith of a muqallid because he lacked rational proof.
2
State the Hanafi position and proof
The Hanafi position is that faith is valid, proven by the mutawatir practice of the Prophet accepting faith from all, including children who cannot reflect.
The passage says: 'فإنه تواتر أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كان يقبل إيمان كل أحد وإن حصل من دون نظر'.
3
Understand the argument about nazar (reflection)
Although some later scholars declared the muqallid sinful for abandoning nazar, the author argues that nazar was only obligatory to attain faith; once faith is obtained, the obligation ceases.
The analogy of jihad: if all disbelievers embrace Islam, jihad drops without sin.
4
Evaluate the counterargument
The claim that the muqallid is sinful because he did not reflect is dismissed; the proof for the validity of his faith is stronger.
The author says: 'وهذا ليس بشيء' (this is nothing).

Key Terms
النظر (al-nazar): التفكر والاستدلال العقلي للوصول إلى الإيمان
تواتر (tawatur): خبر جماعة يستحيل تواطؤهم على الكذب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main proof given for the validity of the muqallid's faith?
A) The Quranic verse commanding belief
B) The mutawatir practice of the Prophet accepting faith from all
C) Logical necessity
D) Consensus of the later scholars

Key Takeaway
The faith of a muqallid is valid, and any obligation to reflect drops once faith is attained.
